**v18** And through your offspring all nations of the earth will be blessed, [^6] because you have obeyed My voice."

**v19** Abraham went back to his servants, and they got up and set out together for Beersheba. And Abraham settled in Beersheba.
#### The Sons of Nahor

**v20** Some time later, Abraham was told, "Milcah has also borne sons to your brother Nahor:
**v21** Uz the firstborn, his brother Buz, Kemuel (the father of Aram),
**v22** Chesed, Hazo, Pildash, Jidlaph, and Bethuel."

**v23** And Bethuel became the father of Rebekah. Milcah bore these eight sons to Abraham's brother Nahor.
**v24** Moreover, Nahor's concubine, whose name was Reumah, bore Tebah, Gaham, Tahash, and Maacah.
[^1]: Or Angel; also in verses 12 and 15 ( 22:11)
[^2]: Or from Me ( 22:12)
[^3]: Most MT manuscripts; other Hebrew manuscripts, SP, LXX, and Syriac saw one ram ( 22:13)
[^4]: Hebrew YHWH Yireh ( 22:14)
[^5]: Cited in Hebrews 6:14 ( 22:17)
[^6]: Cited in Acts 3:25 ( 22:18)

### Chapter 23

#### The Death and Burial of Sarah
**v1** Now Sarah lived to be 127 years old.
**v2** She died in Kiriath-arba (that is, Hebron) in the land of Canaan, and Abraham went out to mourn and to weep for her.

**v3** Then Abraham got up from beside his dead wife and said to the Hittites, [^1]
**v4** "I am a foreigner and an outsider among you. Give me a burial site among you so that I can bury my dead."

**v5** The Hittites replied to Abraham,
**v6** "Listen to us, sir. You are God's chosen one among us. Bury your dead in the finest of our tombs. None of us will withhold his tomb for burying your dead."

**v7** Then Abraham rose and bowed down before the people of the land, the Hittites.
**v8** "If you are willing for me to bury my dead," he said to them, "listen to me, and approach Ephron son of Zohar on my behalf
**v9** to sell me the cave of Machpelah that belongs to him; it is at the end of his field. Let him sell it to me in your presence for full price, so that I may have a burial site."

**v10** Now Ephron was sitting among the sons of Heth. So in the presence of all the Hittites who had come to the gate of his city, Ephron the Hittite answered Abraham,
**v11** "No, my lord. Listen to me. I give you the field, and I give you the cave that is in it. I give it to you in the presence of my people. Bury your dead."

**v12** Again Abraham bowed down before the people of the land
**v13** and said to Ephron in their presence, "If you will please listen to me, I will pay you the price of the field. Accept it from me, so that I may bury my dead there."

**v14** Ephron answered Abraham,
**v15** "Listen to me, my lord. The land is worth four hundred shekels of silver, [^2] but what is that between you and me? Bury your dead."

**v16** Abraham agreed to Ephron's terms and weighed out for him the price he had named in the hearing of the Hittites: four hundred shekels of silver, according to the standard of the merchants.

**v17** So Ephron's field at Machpelah near Mamre, the cave that was in it, and all the trees within the boundaries of the field were deeded over
**v18** to Abraham's possession in the presence of all the Hittites who had come to the gate of his city.
**v19** After this, Abraham buried his wife Sarah in the cave of the field at Machpelah near Mamre (that is, Hebron) in the land of Canaan.
**v20** So the field and its cave were deeded by the Hittites to Abraham as a burial site.
[^1]: Or sons of Heth; also in verses 5, 7, 10, 16, 18, and 20 ( 23:3)
[^2]: 400 shekels is approximately 10.1 pounds or 4.6 kilograms of silver; also in verse 16. ( 23:15)

### Chapter 24

#### A Wife for Isaac
**v1** By now Abraham was old and well along in years, and the LORD had blessed him in every way.
**v2** So Abraham instructed the chief servant of his household, who managed all he owned, "Place your hand under my thigh,
**v3** and I will have you swear by the LORD, the God of heaven and the God of earth, that you will not take a wife for my son from the daughters of the Canaanites among whom I am dwelling,
**v4** but will go to my country and my kindred to take a wife for my son Isaac."

**v5** The servant asked him, "What if the woman is unwilling to follow me to this land? Shall I then take your son back to the land from which you came?"

**v6** Abraham replied, "Make sure that you do not take my son back there.
**v7** The LORD, the God of heaven, who brought me from my father's house and my native land, who spoke to me and promised me on oath, saying, 'To your offspring I will give this land'—He will send His angel before you so that you can take a wife for my son from there.
**v8** And if the woman is unwilling to follow you, then you are released from this oath of mine. Only do not take my son back there."

**v9** So the servant placed his hand under the thigh of his master Abraham and swore an oath to him concerning this matter.

**v10** Then the servant took ten of his master's camels and departed with all manner of good things from his master in hand. And he set out for Nahor's hometown in Aram-naharaim. [^1]
**v11** As evening approached, he made the camels kneel down near the well outside the town at the time when the women went out to draw water.

**v12** "O LORD, God of my master Abraham," he prayed, "please grant me success today, and show kindness to my master Abraham.
**v13** Here I am, standing beside the spring, and the daughters of the townspeople are coming out to draw water.
**v14** Now may it happen that the girl to whom I say, 'Please let down your jar that I may drink,' and who responds, 'Drink, and I will water your camels as well'—let her be the one You have appointed for Your servant Isaac. By this I will know that You have shown kindness to my master."
#### Rebekah Is Chosen

**v15** Before the servant had finished praying, Rebekah came out with her jar on her shoulder. She was the daughter of Bethuel son of Milcah, the wife of Abraham's brother Nahor.
**v16** Now the girl was very beautiful, a virgin who had not had relations with any man. She went down to the spring, filled her jar, and came up again.

**v17** So the servant ran to meet her and said, "Please let me have a little water from your jar."

**v18** "Drink, my lord," she replied, and she quickly lowered her jar to her hands and gave him a drink.

**v19** After she had given him a drink, she said, "I will also draw water for your camels, until they have had enough to drink."
**v20** And she quickly emptied her jar into the trough and ran back to the well to draw water, until she had drawn water for all his camels.

**v21** Meanwhile, the man watched her silently to see whether or not the LORD had made his journey a success.

**v22** And after the camels had finished drinking, he took out a gold ring weighing a beka, [^2] and two gold bracelets for her wrists weighing ten shekels. [^3]
**v23** "Whose daughter are you?" he asked. "Please tell me, is there room in your father's house for us to spend the night?"

**v24** She replied, "I am the daughter of Bethuel, the son that Milcah bore to Nahor."
**v25** Then she added, "We have plenty of straw and feed, as well as a place for you to spend the night."

**v26** Then the man bowed down and worshiped the LORD,
**v27** saying, "Blessed be the LORD, the God of my master Abraham, who has not withheld His kindness and faithfulness from my master. As for me, the LORD has led me on the journey to the house of my master's relatives."

**v28** The girl ran and told her mother's household about these things.
**v29** Now Rebekah had a brother named Laban, and he rushed out to the man at the spring.
**v30** As soon as he saw the ring, and the bracelets on his sister's wrists, and heard Rebekah's words, "The man said this to me," he went and found the man standing by the camels near the spring.

**v31** "Come, you who are blessed by the LORD," said Laban. "Why are you standing out here? I have prepared the house and a place for the camels."
**v32** So the man came to the house, and the camels were unloaded. Straw and feed were brought to the camels, and water to wash his feet and the feet of his companions.

**v33** Then a meal was set before the man, but he said, "I will not eat until I have told you what I came to say." So Laban said, "Please speak."

**v34** "I am Abraham's servant," he replied.
**v35** "The LORD has greatly blessed my master, and he has become rich. He has given him sheep and cattle, silver and gold, menservants and maidservants, camels and donkeys.
**v36** My master's wife Sarah has borne him a son in her old age, and my master has given him everything he owns.

**v37** My master made me swear an oath and said, 'You shall not take a wife for my son from the daughters of the Canaanites in whose land I dwell,
**v38** but you shall go to my father's house and to my kindred to take a wife for my son.'

**v39** Then I asked my master, 'What if the woman will not come back with me?'

**v40** And he told me, 'The LORD, before whom I have walked, will send His angel with you and make your journey a success, so that you may take a wife for my son from my kindred and from my father's house.
**v41** And when you go to my kindred, if they refuse to give her to you, then you will be released from my oath.'

**v42** So when I came to the spring today, I prayed: O LORD, God of my master Abraham, if only You would make my journey a success!
**v43** Here I am, standing beside this spring. Now if a maiden comes out to draw water and I say to her, 'Please let me drink a little water from your jar,'
**v44** and she replies, 'Drink, and I will draw water for your camels as well,' may she be the woman the LORD has appointed for my master's son.

**v45** And before I had finished praying in my heart, there was Rebekah coming out with her jar on her shoulder, and she went down to the spring and drew water. So I said to her, 'Please give me a drink.'

**v46** She quickly lowered her jar from her shoulder and said, 'Drink, and I will water your camels as well.' So I drank, and she also watered the camels.

**v47** Then I asked her, 'Whose daughter are you?' She replied, 'The daughter of Bethuel son of Nahor, whom Milcah bore to him.' So I put the ring on her nose and the bracelets on her wrists.
**v48** Then I bowed down and worshiped the LORD; and I blessed the LORD, the God of my master Abraham, who led me on the right road to take the granddaughter of my master's brother for his son.

**v49** Now if you will show kindness and faithfulness to my master, tell me; but if not, let me know, so that I may go elsewhere."

**v50** Laban and Bethuel answered, "This is from the LORD; we have no choice in the matter.
**v51** Rebekah is here before you. Take her and go, and let her become the wife of your master's son, just as the LORD has decreed."

**v52** When Abraham's servant heard their words, he bowed down to the ground before the LORD.
**v53** Then he brought out jewels of silver and gold, and articles of clothing, and he gave them to Rebekah. He also gave precious gifts to her brother and her mother.
**v54** Then he and the men with him ate and drank and spent the night there.When they got up the next morning, he said, "Send me on my way to my master."

**v55** But her brother and mother said, "Let the girl remain with us ten days or so. After that, she may go."

**v56** But he replied, "Do not delay me, since the LORD has made my journey a success. Send me on my way so that I may go to my master."

**v57** So they said, "We will call the girl and ask her opinion."

**v58** They called Rebekah and asked her, "Will you go with this man?""I will go," she replied.

**v59** So they sent their sister Rebekah on her way, along with her nurse and Abraham's servant and his men.
**v60** And they blessed Rebekah and said to her,"Our sister, may you become the mother of thousands upon thousands.May your offspring possess the gates of their enemies."

**v61** Then Rebekah and her servant girls got ready, mounted the camels, and followed the man. So the servant took Rebekah and left.
#### Isaac Marries Rebekah

**v62** Now Isaac had just returned from Beer-lahai-roi, for he was living in the Negev.
**v63** Early in the evening, Isaac went out to the field to meditate, and looking up, he saw the camels approaching.

**v64** And when Rebekah looked up and saw Isaac, she got down from her camel
**v65** and asked the servant, "Who is that man in the field coming to meet us?""It is my master," the servant answered. So she took her veil and covered herself.
**v66** Then the servant told Isaac all that he had done.

**v67** And Isaac brought her into the tent of his mother Sarah and took Rebekah as his wife. And Isaac loved her and was comforted after his mother's death.
[^1]: That is, Mesopotamia; Aram-naharaim means Aram of the two rivers, likely the region between the Euphrates and Balih Rivers in northwestern Mesopotamia. ( 24:10)
[^2]: A beka is half a shekel, or approximately 0.2 ounces or 5.7 grams. ( 24:22)
[^3]: 10 shekels is approximately 4 ounces or 114 grams. ( 24:22)

### Chapter 25

#### Abraham and Keturah
**v1** Now Abraham had taken another wife, named Keturah,
**v2** and she bore him Zimran, Jokshan, Medan, Midian, Ishbak, and Shuah.

**v3** Jokshan was the father of Sheba and Dedan. And the sons of Dedan were the Asshurites, the Letushites, and the Leummites.

**v4** The sons of Midian were Ephah, Epher, Hanoch, Abida, and Eldaah.All these were descendants of Keturah.

**v5** Abraham left everything he owned to Isaac.
**v6** But while he was still alive, Abraham gave gifts to the sons of his concubines and sent them away from his son Isaac to the land of the east.
#### The Death of Abraham

**v7** Abraham lived a total of 175 years.
**v8** And at a ripe old age he breathed his last and died, old and contented, and was gathered to his people.

**v9** His sons Isaac and Ishmael buried him in the cave of Machpelah near Mamre, in the field of Ephron son of Zohar the Hittite.
**v10** This was the field that Abraham had bought from the Hittites. Abraham was buried there with his wife Sarah.

**v11** After Abraham's death, God blessed his son Isaac, who lived near Beer-lahai-roi.
#### The Descendants of Ishmael

**v12** This is the account of Abraham's son Ishmael, whom Hagar the Egyptian, Sarah's maidservant, bore to Abraham.
**v13** These are the names of the sons of Ishmael in the order of their birth: Nebaioth the firstborn of Ishmael, then Kedar, Adbeel, Mibsam,
**v14** Mishma, Dumah, Massa,
**v15** Hadad, Tema, Jetur, Naphish, and Kedemah.

**v16** These were the sons of Ishmael, and these were their names by their villages and encampments—twelve princes of their tribes.
**v17** Ishmael lived a total of 137 years. Then he breathed his last and died, and was gathered to his people.

**v18** Ishmael's descendants settled from Havilah to Shur, which is near the border of Egypt as you go toward Asshur. [^1] And they lived in hostility toward all their brothers.
#### Jacob and Esau

**v19** This is the account of Abraham's son Isaac. Abraham became the father of Isaac,
**v20** and Isaac was forty years old when he married Rebekah, the daughter of Bethuel the Aramean from Paddan-aram [^2] and the sister of Laban the Aramean.

**v21** Later, Isaac prayed to the LORD on behalf of his wife, because she was barren. And the LORD heard his prayer, and his wife Rebekah conceived.

**v22** But the children inside her struggled with each other, and she said, "Why is this happening to me?" So Rebekah went to inquire of the LORD,
**v23** and He declared to her: "Two nations are in your womb, and two peoples from within you will be separated; one people will be stronger than the other, and the older will serve the younger."[^3]

**v24** When her time came to give birth, there were indeed twins in her womb.
**v25** The first one came out red, covered with hair like a fur coat; so they named him Esau. [^4]
**v26** After this, his brother came out grasping Esau's heel; so he was named Jacob. [^5] And Isaac was sixty years old when the twins were born.

**v27** When the boys grew up, Esau became a skillful hunter, a man of the field, while Jacob was a quiet man who stayed at home.
**v28** Because Isaac had a taste for wild game, he loved Esau; but Rebekah loved Jacob.
#### Esau Sells His Birthright

**v29** One day, while Jacob was cooking some stew, Esau came in from the field and was famished.
**v30** He said to Jacob, "Let me eat some of that red stew, for I am famished." (That is why he was also called Edom. [^6])

**v31** "First sell me your birthright," Jacob replied.

**v32** "Look," said Esau, "I am about to die, so what good is a birthright to me?"

**v33** "Swear to me first," Jacob said.So Esau swore to Jacob and sold him the birthright.
**v34** Then Jacob gave some bread and lentil stew to Esau, who ate and drank and then got up and went away. Thus Esau despised his birthright.
[^1]: Or Assyria ( 25:18)
[^2]: That is, northwest Mesopotamia ( 25:20)
[^3]: Cited in Romans 9:12 ( 25:23)
[^4]: Esau sounds like a Hebrew term that means hairy. ( 25:25)
[^5]: Jacob means he grasps the heel or he deceives. ( 25:26)
[^6]: Edom means red. ( 25:30)

### Chapter 26

#### God's Promise to Isaac
**v1** Now there was another famine in the land, subsequent to the one that had occurred in Abraham's time. And Isaac went to Abimelech king of the Philistines at Gerar.

**v2** The LORD appeared to Isaac and said, "Do not go down to Egypt. Settle in the land where I tell you.
**v3** Stay in this land as a foreigner, and I will be with you and bless you. For I will give all these lands to you and your offspring, and I will confirm the oath that I swore to your father Abraham.
**v4** I will make your descendants as numerous as the stars in the sky, and I will give them all these lands, and through your offspring all nations of the earth will be blessed,
**v5** because Abraham listened to My voice and kept My charge, My commandments, My statutes, and My laws."
#### Isaac Deceives Abimelech

**v6** So Isaac settled in Gerar.
**v7** But when the men of that place asked about his wife, he said, "She is my sister." For he was afraid to say, "She is my wife," since he thought to himself, "The men of this place will kill me on account of Rebekah, because she is so beautiful."

**v8** When Isaac had been there a long time, Abimelech king of the Philistines looked down from the window and was surprised to see Isaac caressing his wife Rebekah.
**v9** Abimelech sent for Isaac and said, "So she is really your wife! How could you say, 'She is my sister'?" Isaac replied, "Because I thought I might die on account of her."

**v10** "What is this you have done to us?" asked Abimelech. "One of the people could easily have slept with your wife, and you would have brought guilt upon us."
**v11** So Abimelech warned all the people, saying, "Whoever harms this man or his wife will surely be put to death."
#### Isaac's Prosperity

**v12** Now Isaac sowed seed in the land, and that very year he reaped a hundredfold. And the LORD blessed him,
**v13** and he became richer and richer, until he was exceedingly wealthy.
**v14** He owned so many flocks and herds and servants that the Philistines envied him.
**v15** So the Philistines took dirt and stopped up all the wells that his father's servants had dug in the days of his father Abraham.

**v16** Then Abimelech said to Isaac, "Depart from us, for you are much too powerful for us."

**v17** So Isaac left that place and encamped in the Valley of Gerar and settled there.
**v18** Isaac reopened the wells that had been dug in the days of his father Abraham, which the Philistines had stopped up after Abraham died. And he gave these wells the same names his father had given them.

**v19** Then Isaac's servants dug in the valley and found a well of fresh water [^1] there.
**v20** But the herdsmen of Gerar quarreled with Isaac's herdsmen and said, "The water is ours!" So he named the well Esek, [^2] because they contended with him.

**v21** Then they dug another well and quarreled over that one also; so he named it Sitnah. [^3]

**v22** He moved on from there and dug another well, and they did not quarrel over it. He named it Rehoboth [^4] and said, "At last the LORD has made room for us, and we will be fruitful in the land."

**v23** From there Isaac went up to Beersheba,
**v24** and that night the LORD appeared to him and said, "I am the God of your father Abraham. Do not be afraid, for I am with you. I will bless you and multiply your descendants for the sake of My servant Abraham."

**v25** So Isaac built an altar there and called on the name of the LORD, and he pitched his tent there. His servants also dug a well there.
#### Isaac's Covenant with Abimelech

**v26** Later, Abimelech came to Isaac from Gerar, with Ahuzzath his adviser and Phicol the commander of his army.

**v27** "Why have you come to me?" Isaac asked them. "You hated me and sent me away."

**v28** "We can plainly see that the LORD has been with you," they replied. "We recommend that there should now be an oath between us and you. Let us make a covenant with you
**v29** that you will not harm us, just as we have not harmed you but have done only good to you, sending you on your way in peace. And now you are blessed by the LORD."

**v30** So Isaac prepared a feast for them, and they ate and drank.
**v31** And they got up early the next morning and swore an oath to each other. Then Isaac sent them on their way, and they left him in peace.

**v32** On that same day, Isaac's servants came and told him about the well they had dug. "We have found water!" they told him.
**v33** So he called it Shibah, [^5] and to this day the name of the city is Beersheba. [^6]
#### Esau's Wives

**v34** When Esau was forty years old, he took as his wives Judith daughter of Beeri the Hittite and Basemath daughter of Elon the Hittite.
**v35** And they brought grief to Isaac and Rebekah.
[^1]: Or flowing water or living water ( 26:19)
[^2]: Esek means contention. ( 26:20)
[^3]: Sitnah means enmity or hostility. ( 26:21)
[^4]: Rehoboth means broad places or open spaces. ( 26:22)
[^5]: Shibah can mean oath or seven. ( 26:33)
[^6]: Beersheba means well of seven or well of the oath. ( 26:33)

### Chapter 27

#### Isaac Blesses Jacob
**v1** When Isaac was old and his eyes were so weak that he could no longer see, he called his older son Esau and said to him, "My son.""Here I am," Esau replied.

**v2** "Look," said Isaac, "I am now old, and I do not know the day of my death.
**v3** Take your weapons—your quiver and bow—and go out into the field to hunt some game for me.
**v4** Then prepare a tasty dish that I love and bring it to me to eat, so that I may bless you before I die."

**v5** Now Rebekah was listening to what Isaac told his son Esau. So when Esau went into the field to hunt game and bring it back,
**v6** Rebekah said to her son Jacob, "Behold, I overheard your father saying to your brother Esau,
**v7** 'Bring me some game and prepare me a tasty dish to eat, so that I may bless you in the presence of the LORD before I die.'

**v8** Now, my son, listen to my voice and do exactly as I tell you.
**v9** Go out to the flock and bring me two choice young goats, so that I can make them into a tasty dish for your father—the kind he loves.
**v10** Then take it to your father to eat, so that he may bless you before he dies."

**v11** Jacob answered his mother Rebekah, "Look, my brother Esau is a hairy man, but I am smooth-skinned.
**v12** What if my father touches me? Then I would be revealed to him as a deceiver, and I would bring upon myself a curse rather than a blessing."

**v13** His mother replied, "Your curse be on me, my son. Just obey my voice and go get them for me."

**v14** So Jacob went and got two goats and brought them to his mother, who made the tasty food his father loved.
**v15** And Rebekah took the finest clothes in the house that belonged to her older son Esau, and she put them on her younger son Jacob.
**v16** She also put the skins of the young goats on his hands and on the smooth part of his neck.
**v17** Then she handed her son Jacob the tasty food and bread she had made.

**v18** So Jacob went to his father and said, "My father.""Here I am!" he answered. "Which one are you, my son?"

**v19** Jacob said to his father, "I am Esau, your firstborn. I have done as you told me. Please sit up and eat some of my game, so that you may bless me."

**v20** But Isaac asked his son, "How did you ever find it so quickly, my son?""Because the LORD your God brought it to me," he replied.

**v21** Then Isaac said to Jacob, "Please come closer so I can touch you, my son. Are you really my son Esau, or not?"

**v22** So Jacob came close to his father Isaac, who touched him and said, "The voice is the voice of Jacob, but the hands are the hands of Esau."
**v23** Isaac did not recognize him, because his hands were hairy like those of his brother Esau; so he blessed him.

**v24** Again he asked, "Are you really my son Esau?" And he replied, "I am."

**v25** "Serve me," said Isaac, "and let me eat some of my son's game, so that I may bless you." Jacob brought it to him, and he ate; then he brought him wine, and he drank.

**v26** Then his father Isaac said to him, "Please come near and kiss me, my son."

**v27** So he came near and kissed him. When Isaac smelled his clothing, he blessed him and said: "Ah, the smell of my sonis like the smell of a fieldthat the LORD has blessed.
**v28** May God give to you the dew of heavenand the richness of the earth—an abundance of grain and new wine.
**v29** May peoples serve you and nations bow down to you. May you be the master of your brothers, and may the sons of your mother bow down to you. May those who curse you be cursed, and those who bless you be blessed."
#### Esau's Lost Hope

**v30** As soon as Isaac had finished blessing him and Jacob had left his father's presence, his brother Esau returned from the hunt.
**v31** He too made some tasty food, brought it to his father, and said to him, "My father, sit up and eat of your son's game, so that you may bless me."

**v32** But his father Isaac replied, "Who are you?""I am Esau, your firstborn son," he answered.

**v33** Isaac began to tremble violently and said, "Who was it, then, who hunted the game and brought it to me? Before you came in, I ate it all and blessed him—and indeed, he will be blessed!"

**v34** When Esau heard his father's words, he let out a loud and bitter cry and said to his father, "Bless me too, O my father!"

**v35** But Isaac replied, "Your brother came deceitfully and took your blessing."

**v36** So Esau declared, "Is he not rightly named Jacob? [^1] For he has cheated me twice. He took my birthright, and now he has taken my blessing." Then he asked, "Haven't you saved a blessing for me?"

**v37** But Isaac answered Esau: "Look, I have made him your master and given him all his relatives as servants; I have sustained him with grain and new wine. What is left that I can do for you, my son?"

**v38** Esau said to his father, "Do you have only one blessing, my father? Bless me too, O my father!" Then Esau wept aloud.

**v39** His father Isaac answered him: "Behold, your dwelling place shall beaway from the richness of the land, away from the dew of heaven above.
**v40** You shall live by the swordand serve your brother.But when you rebel, you will tear his yoke from your neck."

**v41** Esau held a grudge against Jacob because of the blessing his father had given him. And Esau said in his heart, "The days of mourning for my father are at hand; then I will kill my brother Jacob."

**v42** When the words of her older son Esau were relayed to Rebekah, she sent for her younger son Jacob and told him, "Look, your brother Esau is consoling himself by plotting to kill you.
**v43** So now, my son, obey my voice and flee at once to my brother Laban in Haran.
**v44** Stay with him for a while, until your brother's fury subsides—
**v45** until your brother's rage against you wanes and he forgets what you have done to him. Then I will send for you and bring you back from there. Why should I lose both of you in one day?"

**v46** Then Rebekah said to Isaac, "I am weary of my life because of these Hittite women. [^2] If Jacob takes a Hittite wife from among them, what good is my life?"
[^1]: Jacob means he grasps the heel or he deceives. ( 27:36)
[^2]: Or daughters of Heth ( 27:46)

### Chapter 28

#### Jacob's Departure
**v1** So Isaac called for Jacob and blessed him. "Do not take a wife from the Canaanite women," he commanded.
**v2** "Go at once to Paddan-aram, [^1] to the house of your mother's father Bethuel, and take a wife from among the daughters of Laban, your mother's brother.
**v3** May God Almighty [^2] bless you and make you fruitful and multiply you, so that you may become a company of peoples.
**v4** And may He give the blessing of Abraham to you and your descendants, so that you may possess the land where you dwell as a foreigner, the land God gave to Abraham."

**v5** So Isaac sent Jacob to Paddan-aram, to Laban son of Bethuel the Aramean, the brother of Rebekah, who was the mother of Jacob and Esau.
#### Esau Marries Mahalath

**v6** Now Esau learned that Isaac had blessed Jacob and sent him to Paddan-aram to take a wife there, commanding him, "Do not marry a Canaanite woman,"
**v7** and that Jacob had obeyed his father and mother and gone to Paddan-aram.

**v8** And seeing that his father Isaac disapproved of the Canaanite women,
**v9** Esau went to Ishmael and married Mahalath, the sister of Nebaioth and daughter of Abraham's son Ishmael, in addition to the wives he already had.
#### Jacob's Ladder

**v10** Meanwhile Jacob left Beersheba and set out for Haran.
**v11** On reaching a certain place, he spent the night there because the sun had set. And taking one of the stones from that place, he put it under his head and lay down to sleep.

**v12** And Jacob had a dream about a ladder that rested on the earth with its top reaching up to heaven, and God's angels were going up and down the ladder.
**v13** And there at the top [^3] the LORD was standing and saying, "I am the LORD, the God of your father Abraham and the God of Isaac. I will give you and your descendants the land on which you now lie.
**v14** Your descendants will be like the dust of the earth, and you will spread out to the west and east and north and south. All the families of the earth will be blessed through you and your offspring.
**v15** Look, I am with you, and I will watch over you wherever you go, and I will bring you back to this land. For I will not leave you until I have done what I have promised you."

**v16** When Jacob woke up, he said, "Surely the LORD is in this place, and I was unaware of it."
**v17** And he was afraid and said, "How awesome is this place! This is none other than the house of God; this is the gate of heaven!"
#### The Stone of Bethel

**v18** Early the next morning, Jacob took the stone that he had placed under his head, and he set it up as a pillar. He poured oil on top of it,
**v19** and he called that place Bethel, [^4] though previously the city had been named Luz.

**v20** Then Jacob made a vow, saying, "If God will be with me and watch over me on this journey, and if He will provide me with food to eat and clothes to wear,
**v21** so that I may return safely to my father's house, then the LORD will be my God.
**v22** And this stone I have set up as a pillar will be God's house, and of all that You give me I will surely give You a tenth."
[^1]: That is, northwest Mesopotamia; also in verses 5, 6, and 7 ( 28:2)
[^2]: Hebrew El-Shaddai ( 28:3)
[^3]: Or there beside him ( 28:13)
[^4]: Bethel means house of God. ( 28:19)

### Chapter 29

#### Jacob Meets Rachel
**v1** Jacob resumed his journey and came to the land of the people of the east.
**v2** He looked and saw a well in the field, and near it lay three flocks of sheep, because the sheep were watered from this well. And a large stone covered the mouth of the well.
**v3** When all the flocks had been gathered there, the shepherds would roll away the stone from the mouth of the well and water the sheep. Then they would return the stone to its place over the mouth of the well.

**v4** "My brothers," Jacob asked the shepherds, "where are you from?""We are from Haran," they answered.

**v5** "Do you know Laban the grandson of Nahor?" Jacob asked." We know him," they replied.

**v6** "Is he well?" Jacob inquired." Yes," they answered, "and here comes his daughter Rachel with his sheep."

**v7** "Look," said Jacob, "it is still broad daylight; it is not yet time to gather the livestock. Water the sheep and take them back to pasture."

**v8** But they replied, "We cannot, until all the flocks have been gathered and the stone has been rolled away from the mouth of the well. Then we will water the sheep."

**v9** While he was still speaking with them, Rachel arrived with her father's sheep, for she was a shepherdess.
**v10** As soon as Jacob saw Rachel, the daughter of his mother's brother Laban, with Laban's sheep, he went up and rolled the stone away from the mouth of the well and watered his uncle's sheep.
**v11** Then Jacob kissed Rachel and wept aloud.
**v12** He told Rachel that he was Rebekah's son, a relative of her father, and she ran and told her father.

**v13** When Laban heard the news about his sister's son Jacob, he ran out to meet him. He embraced him and kissed him and brought him to his home, where Jacob told him all that had happened.
#### Jacob Marries Leah and Rachel

**v14** Then Laban declared, "You are indeed my own flesh and blood." After Jacob had stayed with him a month,
**v15** Laban said to him, "Just because you are my relative, should you work for nothing? Tell me what your wages should be."

**v16** Now Laban had two daughters; the older was named Leah, and the younger was named Rachel.
**v17** Leah had weak eyes, [^1] but Rachel was shapely and beautiful.
**v18** Since Jacob loved Rachel, he answered, "I will serve you seven years for your younger daughter Rachel."

**v19** Laban replied, "Better that I give her to you than to another. Stay here with me."
**v20** So Jacob served seven years for Rachel, yet it seemed but a few days because of his love for her.

**v21** Finally Jacob said to Laban, "Grant me my wife, for my time is complete, and I want to sleep with her."

**v22** So Laban invited all the men of that place and prepared a feast.
**v23** But when evening came, Laban took his daughter Leah and gave her to Jacob, and he slept with her.
**v24** And Laban gave his servant girl Zilpah to his daughter Leah as her maidservant.

**v25** When morning came, there was Leah! "What have you done to me?" Jacob said to Laban. "Wasn't it for Rachel that I served you? Why have you deceived me?"

**v26** Laban replied, "It is not our custom here to give the younger daughter in marriage before the older.
**v27** Finish this week's celebration, and we will give you the younger one in return for another seven years of work."

**v28** And Jacob did just that. He finished the week's celebration, and Laban gave him his daughter Rachel as his wife.
**v29** Laban also gave his servant girl Bilhah to his daughter Rachel as her maidservant.

**v30** Jacob slept with Rachel as well, and indeed, he loved Rachel more than Leah. So he worked for Laban another seven years.
#### Reuben, Simeon, Levi, and Judah

**v31** When the LORD saw that Leah was unloved, He opened her womb; but Rachel was barren.
**v32** And Leah conceived and gave birth to a son, and she named him Reuben, [^2] for she said, "The LORD has seen my affliction. Surely my husband will love me now."

**v33** Again she conceived and gave birth to a son, and she said, "Because the LORD has heard that I am unloved, He has given me this son as well." So she named him Simeon. [^3]

**v34** Once again Leah conceived and gave birth to a son, and she said, "Now at last my husband will become attached to me, because I have borne him three sons." So he was named Levi. [^4]

**v35** And once more she conceived and gave birth to a son and said, "This time I will praise the LORD." So she named him Judah. [^5] Then Leah stopped having children.
[^1]: Or had delicate eyes ( 29:17)
[^2]: Reuben means Look, a son and also sounds like the Hebrew for He has seen my misery. ( 29:32)
[^3]: Simeon probably means one who hears. ( 29:33)
[^4]: Levi sounds like the Hebrew for being attached to or feeling affection for. ( 29:34)
[^5]: Judah sounds like the Hebrew for praise. ( 29:35)

### Chapter 30

#### Dan and Naphtali
**v1** When Rachel saw that she was not bearing any children for Jacob, she envied her sister. "Give me children, or I will die!" she said to Jacob.

**v2** Jacob became angry with Rachel and said, "Am I in the place of God, who has withheld children from you?"

**v3** Then she said, "Here is my maidservant Bilhah. Sleep with her, that she may bear children for me, [^1] so that through her I too can build a family."

**v4** So Rachel gave Jacob her servant Bilhah as a wife, and he slept with her,
**v5** and Bilhah conceived and bore him a son.
**v6** Then Rachel said, "God has vindicated me; He has heard my plea and given me a son." So she named him Dan. [^2]

**v7** And Rachel's servant Bilhah conceived again and bore Jacob a second son.
**v8** Then Rachel said, "In my great struggles, I have wrestled with my sister and won." So she named him Naphtali. [^3]
#### Gad and Asher

**v9** When Leah saw that she had stopped having children, she gave her servant Zilpah to Jacob as a wife.
**v10** And Leah's servant Zilpah bore Jacob a son.
**v11** Then Leah said, "How fortunate!"[^4] So she named him Gad. [^5]

**v12** When Leah's servant Zilpah bore Jacob a second son,
**v13** Leah said, "How happy I am! For the women call me happy." So she named him Asher. [^6]

**v14** Now during the wheat harvest, Reuben went out and found some mandrakes in the field. When he brought them to his mother, Rachel begged Leah, "Please give me some of your son's mandrakes."

**v15** But Leah replied, "Is it not enough that you have taken away my husband? Now you want to take my son's mandrakes as well?""Very well," said Rachel, "he may sleep with you tonight in exchange for your son's mandrakes."

**v16** When Jacob came in from the field that evening, Leah went out to meet him and said, "You must come with me, for I have hired you with my son's mandrakes." So he slept with her that night.
#### Issachar, Zebulun, and Dinah

**v17** And God listened to Leah, and she conceived and bore a fifth son to Jacob.
**v18** Then Leah said, "God has rewarded me for giving my maidservant to my husband." So she named him Issachar. [^7]

**v19** Again Leah conceived and bore a sixth son to Jacob.
**v20** "God has given me a good gift," she said. "This time my husband will honor me, because I have borne him six sons." And she named him Zebulun. [^8]

**v21** After that, Leah gave birth to a daughter and named her Dinah.
#### Joseph

**v22** Then God remembered Rachel. He listened to her and opened her womb,
**v23** and she conceived and gave birth to a son. "God has taken away my shame," she said.
**v24** She named him Joseph, [^9] and said, "May the LORD add to me another son."
#### Jacob Prospers

**v25** Now after Rachel had given birth to Joseph, Jacob said to Laban, "Send me on my way so I can return to my homeland.
**v26** Give me my wives and children for whom I have served you, that I may go on my way. You know how hard I have worked for you."

**v27** But Laban replied, "If I have found favor in your eyes, please stay. I have learned by divination that the LORD has blessed me because of you."
**v28** And he added, "Name your wages, and I will pay them."

**v29** Then Jacob answered, "You know how I have served you and how your livestock have thrived under my care.
**v30** Indeed, you had very little before my arrival, but now your wealth has increased many times over. The LORD has blessed you wherever I set foot. But now, when may I also provide for my own household?"

**v31** "What can I give you?" Laban asked." You do not need to give me anything," Jacob replied. "If you do this one thing for me, I will keep on shepherding and keeping your flocks.
**v32** Let me go through all your flocks today and remove from them every speckled or spotted sheep, every dark-colored lamb, and every spotted or speckled goat. These will be my wages.
**v33** So my honesty will testify for me when you come to check on my wages in the future. If I have any goats that are not speckled or spotted, or any lambs that are not dark-colored, they will be considered stolen."

**v34** "Agreed," said Laban. "Let it be as you have said."

**v35** That very day Laban removed all the streaked or spotted male goats and every speckled or spotted female goat—every one that had any white on it—and every dark-colored lamb, and he placed them under the care of his sons.
**v36** Then he put a three-day journey between himself and Jacob, while Jacob was shepherding the rest of Laban's flocks.

**v37** Jacob, however, took fresh branches of poplar, almond, and plane trees, and peeled the bark, exposing the white inner wood of the branches.
**v38** Then he set the peeled branches in the watering troughs in front of the flocks coming in to drink. So when the flocks were in heat and came to drink,
**v39** they mated in front of the branches. And they bore young that were streaked or speckled or spotted.
**v40** Jacob set apart the young, but made the rest face the streaked dark-colored sheep in Laban's flocks. Then he set his own stock apart and did not put them with Laban's animals.

**v41** Whenever the stronger females of the flock were in heat, Jacob would place the branches in the troughs, in full view of the animals, so that they would breed in front of the branches.
**v42** But if the animals were weak, he did not set out the branches. So the weaker animals went to Laban and the stronger ones to Jacob.

**v43** Thus Jacob became exceedingly prosperous. He owned large flocks, maidservants and menservants, and camels and donkeys.
[^1]: Literally bear children on my knees ( 30:3)
[^2]: Dan means He has judged or He has vindicated. ( 30:6)
[^3]: Naphtali sounds like the Hebrew for wrestling. ( 30:8)
[^4]: Alternate MT reading (see also LXX); the other alternate reads "A troop is coming!" ( 30:11)
[^5]: Gad sounds like the Hebrew for good fortune, or alternately for band of raiders. ( 30:11)
[^6]: Asher means happy. ( 30:13)
[^7]: Issachar sounds like the Hebrew for wages or reward. ( 30:18)
[^8]: Zebulun sounds like the Hebrew for honor. ( 30:20)
[^9]: Joseph means may He add. ( 30:24)

### Chapter 31

#### Jacob Flees from Laban
**v1** Now Jacob heard that Laban's sons were saying, "Jacob has taken away all that belonged to our father and built all this wealth at our father's expense."
**v2** And Jacob saw from the countenance of Laban that his attitude toward him had changed.

**v3** Then the LORD said to Jacob, "Go back to the land of your fathers and to your kindred, and I will be with you."

**v4** So Jacob sent word and called Rachel and Leah to the field where his flocks were,
**v5** and he told them, "I can see from your father's countenance that his attitude toward me has changed; but the God of my father has been with me.
**v6** You know that I have served your father with all my strength.
**v7** And although he has cheated me and changed my wages ten times, God has not allowed him to harm me.
**v8** If he said, 'The speckled will be your wages,' then the whole flock bore speckled offspring. If he said, 'The streaked will be your wages,' then the whole flock bore streaked offspring.
**v9** Thus God has taken away your father's livestock and given them to me.

**v10** When the flocks were breeding, I saw in a dream that the streaked, spotted, and speckled males were mating with the females.
**v11** In that dream the angel [^1] of God said to me, 'Jacob!' And I replied, 'Here I am.'

**v12** 'Look up,' he said, 'and see that all the males that are mating with the flock are streaked, spotted, or speckled; for I have seen all that Laban has done to you.
**v13** I am the God of Bethel, where you anointed the pillar and made a solemn vow to Me. Now get up, leave this land at once, and return to your native land.'"

**v14** And Rachel and Leah replied, "Do we have any portion or inheritance left in our father's house?
**v15** Are we not regarded by him as outsiders? Not only has he sold us, but he has certainly squandered what was paid for us.
**v16** Surely all the wealth that God has taken away from our father belongs to us and to our children. So do whatever God has told you."

**v17** Then Jacob got up and put his children and his wives on camels,
**v18** and he drove all his livestock before him, along with all the possessions he had acquired in Paddan-aram, [^2] to go to his father Isaac in the land in Canaan.

**v19** Now while Laban was out shearing his sheep, Rachel stole her father's household idols.
**v20** Moreover, Jacob deceived [^3] Laban the Aramean by not telling him that he was running away.
**v21** So he fled with all his possessions, crossed the Euphrates, [^4] and headed for the hill country of Gilead.
#### Laban Pursues Jacob

**v22** On the third day Laban was informed that Jacob had fled.
**v23** So he took his relatives with him, pursued Jacob for seven days, and overtook him in the hill country of Gilead.
**v24** But that night God came to Laban the Aramean in a dream and warned him, "Be careful not to say anything to Jacob, either good or bad."

**v25** Now Jacob had pitched his tent in the hill country of Gilead when Laban overtook him, and Laban and his relatives camped there as well.
**v26** Then Laban said to Jacob, "What have you done? You have deceived me and carried off my daughters like captives of war!
**v27** Why did you run away secretly and deceive me, without even telling me? I would have sent you away with joy and singing, with tambourines and harps.
**v28** But you did not even let me kiss my grandchildren and my daughters goodbye. Now you have done a foolish thing.

**v29** I have power to do you great harm, but last night the God of your father said to me, 'Be careful not to say anything to Jacob, either good or bad.'
**v30** Now you have gone off because you long for your father's house. But why have you stolen my gods?"

**v31** "I was afraid," Jacob answered, "for I thought you would take your daughters from me by force.
**v32** If you find your gods with anyone here, he shall not live! In the presence of our relatives, see for yourself if anything is yours, and take it back." For Jacob did not know that Rachel had stolen the idols.

**v33** So Laban went into Jacob's tent, then Leah's tent, and then the tents of the two maidservants, but he found nothing. Then he left Leah's tent and entered Rachel's tent.
**v34** Now Rachel had taken Laban's household idols, put them in the saddlebag of her camel, and was sitting on them. And Laban searched everything in the tent but found nothing.

**v35** Rachel said to her father, "Sir, do not be angry that I cannot stand up before you; for I am having my period." So Laban searched but could not find the household idols.

**v36** Then Jacob became incensed and challenged Laban. "What is my crime?" he said. "For what sin of mine have you so hotly pursued me?
**v37** You have searched all my goods! Have you found anything that belongs to you? Put it here before my brothers and yours, that they may judge between the two of us.

**v38** I have been with you for twenty years now. Your sheep and goats have not miscarried, nor have I eaten the rams of your flock.
**v39** I did not bring you anything torn by wild beasts; I bore the loss myself. And you demanded payment from me for what was stolen by day or night.
**v40** As it was, the heat consumed me by day and the frost by night, and sleep fled from my eyes.

**v41** Thus for twenty years I have served in your household—fourteen years for your two daughters and six years for your flocks—and you have changed my wages ten times!
**v42** If the God of my father, the God of Abraham and the Fear of Isaac, had not been with me, surely by now you would have sent me away empty-handed. But God has seen my affliction and the toil of my hands, and last night He rendered judgment."
#### Jacob's Covenant with Laban

**v43** But Laban answered Jacob, "These daughters are my daughters, these sons are my sons, and these flocks are my flocks! Everything you see is mine! Yet what can I do today about these daughters of mine or the children they have borne?
**v44** Come now, let us make a covenant, you and I, and let it serve as a witness between you and me."

**v45** So Jacob picked out a stone and set it up as a pillar,
**v46** and he said to his relatives, "Gather some stones." So they took stones and made a mound, and there by the mound they ate.
**v47** Laban called it Jegar-sahadutha, and Jacob called it Galeed. [^5]

**v48** Then Laban declared, "This mound is a witness between you and me this day." Therefore the place was called Galeed.
**v49** It was also called Mizpah, [^6] because Laban said, "May the LORD keep watch between you and me when we are absent from each other.
**v50** If you mistreat my daughters or take other wives, although no one is with us, remember that God is a witness between you and me."

**v51** Laban also said to Jacob, "Here is the mound, and here is the pillar I have set up between you and me.
**v52** This mound is a witness, and this pillar is a witness, that I will not go past this mound to harm you, and you will not go past this mound and pillar to harm me.
**v53** May the God of Abraham and the God of Nahor, the God of their father, judge between us." So Jacob swore by the Fear of his father Isaac.

**v54** Then Jacob offered a sacrifice on the mountain and invited his relatives to eat a meal. And after they had eaten, they spent the night on the mountain.
**v55** Early the next morning, Laban got up and kissed his grandchildren and daughters and blessed them. Then he left to return home.
[^1]: Or Angel ( 31:11)
[^2]: That is, northwest Mesopotamia ( 31:18)
[^3]: Or stole the heart of; also in verses 26 and 27 ( 31:20)
[^4]: Hebrew the River ( 31:21)
[^5]: The Aramaic Jegar-sahadutha and the Hebrew Galeed both mean heap of witnesses. ( 31:47)
[^6]: Mizpah means watchtower. ( 31:49)

### Chapter 32

#### Jacob Prepares to Meet Esau
**v1** Jacob also went on his way, and the angels of God met him.
**v2** When Jacob saw them, he said, "This is the camp of God." So he named that place Mahanaim. [^1]

**v3** Jacob sent messengers ahead of him to his brother Esau in the land of Seir, the country of Edom.
**v4** He instructed them, "You are to say to my master Esau, 'Your servant Jacob says: I have been staying with Laban and have remained there until now.
**v5** I have oxen, donkeys, flocks, menservants, and maidservants. I have sent this message to inform my master, so that I may find favor in your sight.'"

**v6** When the messengers returned to Jacob, they said, "We went to your brother Esau, and now he is coming to meet you—he and four hundred men with him."

**v7** In great fear and distress, Jacob divided his people into two camps, as well as the flocks and herds and camels.
**v8** He thought, "If Esau comes and attacks one camp, then the other camp can escape."

**v9** Then Jacob declared, "O God of my father Abraham, God of my father Isaac, the LORD who told me, 'Go back to your country and to your kindred, and I will make you prosper,'
**v10** I am unworthy of all the kindness and faithfulness You have shown Your servant. Indeed, with only my staff I came across the Jordan, but now I have become two camps.
**v11** Please deliver me from the hand of my brother Esau, for I am afraid that he may come and attack me and the mothers and children with me.
**v12** But You have said, 'I will surely make you prosper, and I will make your offspring like the sand of the sea, too numerous to count.'"

**v13** Jacob spent the night there, and from what he had brought with him, he selected a gift for his brother Esau:
**v14** 200 female goats, 20 male goats, 200 ewes, 20 rams,
**v15** 30 milk camels with their young, 40 cows, 10 bulls, 20 female donkeys, and 10 male donkeys.
**v16** He entrusted them to his servants in separate herds and told them, "Go on ahead of me, and keep some distance between the herds."

**v17** He instructed the one in the lead, "When my brother Esau meets you and asks, 'To whom do you belong, where are you going, and whose animals are these before you?'
**v18** then you are to say, 'They belong to your servant Jacob. They are a gift, sent to my lord Esau. And behold, Jacob is behind us.'"

**v19** He also instructed the second, the third, and all those following behind the herds: "When you meet Esau, you are to say the same thing to him.
**v20** You are also to say, 'Look, your servant Jacob is right behind us.'" For he thought, "I will appease Esau [^2] with the gift that is going before me. After that I can face him, and perhaps he will accept me. [^3]"

**v21** So Jacob's gifts went on before him, while he spent the night in the camp.
#### Jacob Wrestles with God

**v22** During the night Jacob got up and took his two wives, his two maidservants, and his eleven sons, and crossed the ford of the Jabbok.
**v23** He took them and sent them across the stream, along with all his possessions.

**v24** So Jacob was left all alone, and there a man [^4] wrestled with him until daybreak.
**v25** When the man saw that he could not overpower Jacob, he struck the socket of Jacob's hip and dislocated it as they wrestled.
**v26** Then the man said, "Let me go, for it is daybreak." But Jacob replied, "I will not let you go unless you bless me."

**v27** "What is your name?" the man asked." Jacob," he replied.

**v28** Then the man said, "Your name will no longer be Jacob, [^5] but Israel, [^6] because you have struggled with God and with men, and you have prevailed."

**v29** And Jacob requested, "Please tell me your name." But he replied, "Why do you ask my name?" Then he blessed Jacob there.

**v30** So Jacob named the place Peniel, [^7] saying, "Indeed, I have seen God face to face, and yet my life was spared."

**v31** The sun rose above him as he passed by Penuel, [^8] and he was limping because of his hip.
**v32** Therefore to this day the Israelites do not eat the tendon attached to the socket of the hip, because the socket of Jacob's hip was struck near that tendon.
[^1]: Mahanaim means two camps. ( 32:2)
[^2]: Or I will appease his face ( 32:20)
[^3]: Literally perhaps he will lift up my face ( 32:20)
[^4]: Or Man; here and in verses 25–28; corresponding pronouns may also be capitalized ( 32:24)
[^5]: Jacob means he grasps the heel or he deceives. ( 32:28)
[^6]: Israel means he struggles with God. ( 32:28)
[^7]: Peniel means the face of God. ( 32:30)
[^8]: Penuel is a variant of Peniel; see verse 30. ( 32:31)

### Chapter 33

#### Jacob Meets Esau
**v1** Now Jacob looked up and saw Esau coming toward him with four hundred men. So he divided the children among Leah, Rachel, and the two maidservants.
**v2** He put the maidservants and their children in front, Leah and her children next, and Rachel and Joseph at the rear.
**v3** But Jacob himself went on ahead and bowed to the ground seven times as he approached his brother.

**v4** Esau, however, ran to him and embraced him, threw his arms around his neck, and kissed him. And they both wept.

**v5** When Esau looked up and saw the women and children, he asked, "Who are these with you?" Jacob answered, "These are the children God has graciously given your servant."
**v6** Then the maidservants and their children approached and bowed down.
**v7** Leah and her children also approached and bowed down, and then Joseph and Rachel approached and bowed down.

**v8** "What do you mean by sending this whole company to meet me?" asked Esau." To find favor in your sight, my lord," Jacob answered.

**v9** "I already have plenty, my brother," Esau replied. "Keep what belongs to you."

**v10** But Jacob insisted, "No, please! If I have found favor in your sight, then receive this gift from my hand. For indeed, I have seen your face, and it is like seeing the face of God, since you have received me favorably.
**v11** Please accept my gift [^1] that was brought to you, because God has been gracious to me and I have all I need." So Jacob pressed him until he accepted.

**v12** Then Esau said, "Let us be on our way, and I will go ahead of you."

**v13** But Jacob replied, "My lord knows that the children are frail, and I must care for sheep and cattle that are nursing their young. If they are driven hard for even a day, all the animals will die.
**v14** Please let my lord go ahead of his servant. I will continue on slowly, at a comfortable pace for the livestock and children, until I come to my lord at Seir."

**v15** "Let me leave some of my people with you," Esau said.But Jacob replied, "Why do that? Let me find favor in the sight of my lord."

**v16** So that day Esau started on his way back to Seir,
**v17** but Jacob went on to Succoth, [^2] where he built a house for himself and shelters for his livestock; that is why the place was called Succoth.
#### Jacob Settles in Shechem

**v18** After Jacob had come from Paddan-aram, [^3] he arrived safely at the city of Shechem in the land of Canaan, and he camped just outside the city.
**v19** And the plot of ground where he pitched his tent, he purchased from the sons of Hamor, Shechem's father, for a hundred pieces of silver. [^4]
**v20** There he set up an altar and called it El-Elohe-Israel. [^5]
[^1]: Or blessing or treaty of peace ( 33:11)
[^2]: Succoth means booths or shelters or tabernacles; twice in this verse. ( 33:17)
[^3]: That is, northwest Mesopotamia ( 33:18)
[^4]: Hebrew a hundred kesitahs; the value or weight of the kesitah is no longer known ( 33:19)
[^5]: El-Elohe-Israel means God is the God of Israel or mighty is the God of Israel. ( 33:20)

### Chapter 34

#### The Defiling of Dinah
**v1** Now Dinah, the daughter Leah had borne to Jacob, went out to visit the daughters of the land.
**v2** When Shechem son of Hamor the Hivite, the prince of the region, saw her, he took her and lay with her by force.
**v3** And his soul was drawn to Dinah, the daughter of Jacob. He loved the young girl and spoke to her tenderly.
**v4** So Shechem told his father Hamor, "Get me this girl as a wife."

**v5** Jacob heard that Shechem had defiled his daughter Dinah, but since his sons were with his livestock in the field, he remained silent about it until they returned.
**v6** Meanwhile, Shechem's father Hamor came to speak with Jacob.
**v7** When Jacob's sons heard what had happened, they returned from the field. They were filled with grief and fury, because Shechem had committed an outrage in Israel [^1] by lying with Jacob's daughter—a thing that should not be done.

**v8** But Hamor said to them, "My son Shechem longs for your daughter. Please give her to him as his wife.
**v9** Intermarry with us; give us your daughters and take our daughters for yourselves.
**v10** You may settle among us, and the land will be open to you. Live here, move about freely, and acquire your own property."

**v11** Then Shechem said to Dinah's father and brothers, "Grant me this favor, and I will give you whatever you ask.
**v12** Demand a high dowry and an expensive gift, and I will give you whatever you ask. Only give me the girl as my wife!"
#### The Revenge of Dinah's Brothers

**v13** But because Shechem had defiled their sister Dinah, Jacob's sons answered him and his father Hamor deceitfully.
**v14** "We cannot do such a thing," they said. "To give our sister to an uncircumcised man would be a disgrace to us.
**v15** We will consent to this on one condition, that you become circumcised like us—every one of your males.
**v16** Then we will give you our daughters and take your daughters for ourselves. We will dwell among you and become one people.
**v17** But if you will not agree to be circumcised, then we will take our sister and go."

**v18** Their offer seemed good to Hamor and his son Shechem.
**v19** The young man, who was the most respected of all his father's household, did not hesitate to fulfill this request, because he was delighted with Jacob's daughter.

**v20** So Hamor and his son Shechem went to the gate of their city and addressed the men of their city:
**v21** "These men are at peace with us. Let them live and trade in our land; indeed, it is large enough for them. Let us take their daughters in marriage and give our daughters to them.
**v22** But only on this condition will the men agree to dwell with us and be one people: if all our men are circumcised as they are.
**v23** Will not their livestock, their possessions, and all their animals become ours? Only let us consent to them, and they will dwell among us."

**v24** All the men who went out of the city gate listened to Hamor and his son Shechem, and every male of the city was circumcised.

**v25** Three days later, while they were still in pain, two of Jacob's sons (Dinah's brothers Simeon and Levi) took their swords, went into the unsuspecting city, and slaughtered every male.
**v26** They killed Hamor and his son Shechem with their swords, took Dinah out of Shechem's house, and went away.

**v27** Jacob's other sons came upon the slaughter and looted the city, because their sister had been defiled.
**v28** They took their flocks and herds and donkeys, and everything else in the city or in the field.
**v29** They carried off all their possessions and women and children, and they plundered everything in their houses.

**v30** Then Jacob said to Simeon and Levi, "You have brought trouble upon me by making me a stench to the Canaanites and Perizzites, the people of this land. We are few in number; if they unite against me and attack me, I and my household will be destroyed."

**v31** But they replied, "Should he have treated our sister like a prostitute?"
[^1]: Or against Israel ( 34:7)

### Chapter 35

#### Jacob Returns to Bethel
**v1** Then God said to Jacob, "Arise, go up to Bethel, and settle there. Build an altar there to the God who appeared to you when you fled from your brother Esau."

**v2** So Jacob told his household and all who were with him, "Get rid of the foreign gods that are among you. Purify yourselves and change your garments.
**v3** Then let us arise and go to Bethel. I will build an altar there to God, who answered me in my day of distress. He has been with me wherever I have gone."

**v4** So they gave Jacob all their foreign gods and all their earrings, and Jacob buried them under the oak [^1] near Shechem.

**v5** As they set out, a terror from God fell over the surrounding cities, so that they did not pursue Jacob's sons.
**v6** So Jacob and everyone with him arrived in Luz (that is, Bethel) in the land of Canaan.
**v7** There Jacob built an altar, and he called that place El-bethel, [^2] because it was there that God had revealed Himself to Jacob as he fled from his brother.

**v8** Now Deborah, Rebekah's nurse, died and was buried under the oak [^3] below Bethel. So Jacob named it Allon-bacuth. [^4]

**v9** After Jacob had returned from Paddan-aram, [^5] God appeared to him again and blessed him.
**v10** And God said to him, "Though your name is Jacob, [^6] you will no longer be called Jacob. Instead, your name will be Israel. [^7]" So God named him Israel.

**v11** And God told him, "I am God Almighty. [^8] Be fruitful and multiply. A nation—even a company of nations—shall come from you, and kings shall descend from you.
**v12** The land that I gave to Abraham and Isaac I will give to you, and I will give this land to your descendants after you."

**v13** Then God went up from the place where He had spoken with him.

**v14** So Jacob set up a pillar in the place where God had spoken with him—a stone marker—and he poured out a drink offering on it and anointed it with oil.
**v15** Jacob called the place where God had spoken with him Bethel. [^9]
#### Benjamin Born, Rachel Dies

**v16** Later, they set out from Bethel, and while they were still some distance from Ephrath, Rachel began to give birth, and her labor was difficult.
**v17** During her severe labor, the midwife said to her, "Do not be afraid, for you are having another son."

**v18** And with her last breath—for she was dying—she named him Ben-oni. [^10] But his father called him Benjamin. [^11]

**v19** So Rachel died and was buried on the way to Ephrath (that is, Bethlehem).
**v20** Jacob set up a pillar on her grave; it marks Rachel's tomb to this day.
#### The Sons of Jacob

**v21** Israel again set out and pitched his tent beyond the Tower of Eder.
**v22** While Israel was living in that region, Reuben went in and slept with his father's concubine Bilhah, and Israel heard about it.Jacob had twelve sons:

**v23** The sons of Leah were Reuben the firstborn of Jacob, Simeon, Levi, Judah, Issachar, and Zebulun.

**v24** The sons of Rachel were Joseph and Benjamin.

**v25** The sons of Rachel's maidservant Bilhah were Dan and Naphtali.

**v26** And the sons of Leah's maidservant Zilpah were Gad and Asher.These are the sons of Jacob, who were born to him in Paddan-aram.
#### The Death of Isaac

**v27** Jacob returned to his father Isaac at Mamre, near Kiriath-arba (that is, Hebron), where Abraham and Isaac had stayed.

**v28** And Isaac lived 180 years.
**v29** Then he breathed his last and died and was gathered to his people, old and full of years. And his sons Esau and Jacob buried him.
[^1]: Or terebinth or great tree ( 35:4)
[^2]: El-bethel means God of Bethel. ( 35:7)
[^3]: Or great tree ( 35:8)
[^4]: Allon-bacuth means oak of weeping. ( 35:8)
[^5]: That is, northwest Mesopotamia; also in verse 26 ( 35:9)
[^6]: Jacob means he grasps the heel or he deceives. ( 35:10)
[^7]: Israel means he struggles with God. ( 35:10)
[^8]: Hebrew El-Shaddai ( 35:11)
[^9]: Bethel means house of God. ( 35:15)
[^10]: Ben-oni could mean son of my sorrow or son of my strength. ( 35:18)
[^11]: Benjamin means son of my right hand. ( 35:18)

### Chapter 36

#### The Descendants of Esau
**v1** This is the account of Esau (that is, Edom).
**v2** Esau took his wives from the daughters of Canaan: Adah daughter of Elon the Hittite, Oholibamah daughter of Anah and granddaughter of Zibeon the Hivite,
**v3** and Basemath daughter of Ishmael and sister of Nebaioth.
**v4** And Adah bore Eliphaz to Esau, Basemath gave birth to Reuel,
**v5** and Oholibamah gave birth to Jeush, Jalam, and Korah. These were the sons of Esau, who were born to him in the land of Canaan.

**v6** Later, Esau took his wives and sons and daughters and all the people of his household, along with his livestock, all his other animals, and all the property he had acquired in Canaan, and he moved to a land far away from his brother Jacob.
**v7** For their possessions were too great for them to dwell together; the land where they stayed could not support them because of their livestock.
**v8** So Esau (that is, Edom) settled in the area of Mount Seir.

**v9** This is the account of Esau, the father of the Edomites, in the area of Mount Seir.

**v10** These are the names of Esau's sons: Eliphaz son of Esau's wife Adah, and Reuel son of Esau's wife Basemath.

**v11** The sons of Eliphaz were Teman, Omar, Zepho, Gatam, and Kenaz.
**v12** Additionally, Timna, a concubine of Esau's son Eliphaz, gave birth to Amalek. These are the grandsons of Esau's wife Adah.

**v13** These are the sons of Reuel: Nahath, Zerah, Shammah, and Mizzah. They are the grandsons of Esau's wife Basemath.

**v14** These are the sons of Esau's wife Oholibamah (daughter of Anah and granddaughter of Zibeon) whom she bore to Esau: Jeush, Jalam, and Korah.

**v15** These are the chiefs among the sons of Esau. The sons of Eliphaz the firstborn of Esau: Chiefs Teman, Omar, Zepho, Kenaz,
**v16** Korah, [^1] Gatam, and Amalek. They are the chiefs of Eliphaz in the land of Edom, and they are the grandsons of Adah.

**v17** These are the sons of Esau's son Reuel: Chiefs Nahath, Zerah, Shammah, and Mizzah. They are the chiefs descended from Reuel in the land of Edom, and they are the grandsons of Esau's wife Basemath.

**v18** These are the sons of Esau's wife Oholibamah: Chiefs Jeush, Jalam, and Korah. They are the chiefs descended from Esau's wife Oholibamah, the daughter of Anah.

**v19** All these are the sons of Esau (that is, Edom), and they were their chiefs.
#### The Descendants of Seir

**v20** These are the sons of Seir the Horite, who were living in the land: Lotan, Shobal, Zibeon, Anah,
**v21** Dishon, Ezer, and Dishan. They are the chiefs of the Horites, the descendants of Seir in the land of Edom.

**v22** The sons of Lotan were Hori and Hemam. [^2] Timna was Lotan's sister.

**v23** These are the sons of Shobal: Alvan, Manahath, Ebal, Shepho, and Onam.

**v24** These are the sons of Zibeon: Aiah and Anah. (This is the Anah who found the hot springs in the wilderness as he was pasturing the donkeys of his father Zibeon.)

**v25** These are the children of Anah: Dishon and Oholibamah daughter of Anah.

**v26** These are the sons of Dishon: [^3] Hemdan, Eshban, Ithran, and Cheran.

**v27** These are the sons of Ezer: Bilhan, Zaavan, and Akan.

**v28** These are the sons of Dishan: Uz and Aran.

**v29** These are the chiefs of the Horites: Chiefs Lotan, Shobal, Zibeon, Anah,
**v30** Dishon, Ezer, and Dishan. They are the chiefs of the Horites, according to their divisions in the land of Seir.
#### The Kings of Edom

**v31** These are the kings who reigned in the land of Edom before any king reigned over the Israelites: [^4]

**v32** Bela son of Beor reigned in Edom; the name of his city was Dinhabah.

**v33** When Bela died, Jobab son of Zerah from Bozrah reigned in his place.

**v34** When Jobab died, Husham from the land of the Temanites reigned in his place.

**v35** When Husham died, Hadad son of Bedad, who defeated Midian in the country of Moab, reigned in his place. And the name of his city was Avith.

**v36** When Hadad died, Samlah from Masrekah reigned in his place.

**v37** When Samlah died, Shaul from Rehoboth on the Euphrates [^5] reigned in his place.

**v38** When Shaul died, Baal-hanan son of Achbor reigned in his place.

**v39** When Baal-hanan son of Achbor died, Hadad [^6] reigned in his place. His city was named Pau, and his wife's name was Mehetabel daughter of Matred, the daughter of Me-zahab.

**v40** These are the names of Esau's chiefs, according to their families and regions, by their names: Chiefs Timna, Alvah, Jetheth,
**v41** Oholibamah, Elah, Pinon,
**v42** Kenaz, Teman, Mibzar,
**v43** Magdiel, and Iram. These were the chiefs of Edom, according to their settlements in the land they possessed. Esau was the father of the Edomites.
[^1]: Hebrew; SP (also in verse 11 and 1 Chronicles 1:36) does not include Korah. ( 36:16)
[^2]: Hemam is a variant of Homam; see 1 Chronicles 1:39. ( 36:22)
[^3]: Hebrew Dishan, a variant of Dishon ( 36:26)
[^4]: Or before an Israelite king reigned over them: ( 36:31)
[^5]: Hebrew the River ( 36:37)
[^6]: Some MT manuscripts, SP, and Syriac (see also 1 Chronicles 1:50); other MT manuscripts Hadar ( 36:39)

### Chapter 37

#### Joseph's Dreams
**v1** Now Jacob lived in the land where his father had resided, the land of Canaan.

**v2** This is the account of Jacob. When Joseph was seventeen years old, he was tending the flock with his brothers, the sons of his father's wives Bilhah and Zilpah, and he brought their father a bad report about them.

**v3** Now Israel loved Joseph more than his other sons, because Joseph had been born to him in his old age; so he made him a robe of many colors. [^1]
**v4** When Joseph's brothers saw that their father loved him more than any of them, they hated him and could not speak a kind word to him.

**v5** Then Joseph had a dream, and when he told it to his brothers, they hated him even more.
**v6** He said to them, "Listen to this dream I had:
**v7** We were binding sheaves of grain in the field, and suddenly my sheaf rose and stood upright, while your sheaves gathered around and bowed down to mine."

**v8** "Do you intend to reign over us?" his brothers asked. "Will you actually rule us?" So they hated him even more because of his dream and his statements.

**v9** Then Joseph had another dream and told it to his brothers. "Look," he said, "I had another dream, and this time the sun and moon and eleven stars were bowing down to me."

**v10** He told his father and brothers, but his father rebuked him and said, "What is this dream that you have had? Will your mother and brothers and I actually come and bow down to the ground before you?"
**v11** And his brothers were jealous of him, but his father kept in mind what he had said.
#### Joseph Sold into Egypt

**v12** Some time later, Joseph's brothers had gone to pasture their father's flocks near Shechem.
**v13** Israel said to him, "Are not your brothers pasturing the flocks at Shechem? Get ready; I am sending you to them.""I am ready," Joseph replied.

**v14** Then Israel told him, "Go now and see how your brothers and the flocks are faring, and bring word back to me." So he sent him off from the Valley of Hebron. And when Joseph arrived in Shechem,
**v15** a man found him wandering in the field and asked, "What are you looking for?"

**v16** "I am looking for my brothers," Joseph replied. "Can you please tell me where they are pasturing their flocks?"

**v17** "They have moved on from here," the man answered. "I heard them say, 'Let us go to Dothan.'" So Joseph set out after his brothers and found them at Dothan.

**v18** Now Joseph's brothers saw him in the distance, and before he arrived, they plotted to kill him.
**v19** "Here comes that dreamer!" they said to one another.
**v20** "Come now, let us kill him and throw him into one of the pits. We can say that a vicious animal has devoured him. Then we shall see what becomes of his dreams!"

**v21** When Reuben heard this, he tried to rescue Joseph from their hands. "Let us not take his life," he said.
**v22** "Do not shed his blood. Throw him into this pit in the wilderness, but do not lay a hand on him." Reuben said this so that he could rescue Joseph from their hands and return him to his father.

**v23** So when Joseph came to his brothers, they stripped him of his robe—the robe of many colors he was wearing—
**v24** and they took him and threw him into the pit. Now the pit was empty, with no water in it.

**v25** And as they sat down to eat a meal, they looked up and saw a caravan of Ishmaelites coming from Gilead. Their camels were carrying spices, balm, and myrrh on their way down to Egypt.

**v26** Then Judah said to his brothers, "What profit will we gain if we kill our brother and cover up his blood?
**v27** Come, let us sell him to the Ishmaelites and not lay a hand on him; for he is our brother, our own flesh." And they agreed.
**v28** So when the Midianite traders passed by, his brothers pulled Joseph out of the pit and sold him for twenty shekels of silver [^2] to the Ishmaelites, who took him to Egypt.

**v29** When Reuben returned to the pit and saw that Joseph was not there, he tore his clothes,
**v30** returned to his brothers, and said, "The boy is gone! What am I going to do?"
#### Jacob Mourns Joseph

**v31** Then they took Joseph's robe, slaughtered a young goat, and dipped the robe in its blood.
**v32** They sent the robe of many colors to their father and said, "We found this. Examine it to see whether it is your son's robe or not."

**v33** His father recognized it and said, "It is my son's robe! A vicious animal has devoured him. Joseph has surely been torn to pieces!"
**v34** Then Jacob tore his clothes, put sackcloth around his waist, and mourned for his son many days.
**v35** All his sons and daughters tried to comfort him, but he refused to be comforted. "No," he said. "I will go down to Sheol mourning for my son." So his father wept for him.

**v36** Meanwhile, the Midianites [^3] sold Joseph in Egypt to Potiphar, an officer of Pharaoh and captain of the guard.
[^1]: Possibly a robe with long sleeves; also in verses 23 and 32 ( 37:3)
[^2]: 20 shekels is approximately 8 ounces or 228 grams of silver. ( 37:28)
[^3]: Hebrew the Medanites ( 37:36)

### Chapter 38

#### Judah and Tamar
**v1** About that time, Judah left his brothers and settled near a man named Hirah, an Adullamite.
**v2** There Judah saw the daughter of a Canaanite man named Shua, and he took her as a wife and slept with her.
**v3** So she conceived and gave birth to a son, and Judah named him Er.
**v4** Again she conceived and gave birth to a son, and she named him Onan.
**v5** Then she gave birth to another son and named him Shelah; it was at Chezib that she gave birth to him.

**v6** Now Judah acquired a wife for Er, his firstborn, and her name was Tamar.
**v7** But Er, Judah's firstborn, was wicked in the sight of the LORD; so the LORD put him to death.
**v8** Then Judah said to Onan, "Sleep with your brother's wife. Perform your duty as her brother-in-law and raise up offspring for your brother."

**v9** But Onan knew that the offspring would not belong to him; so whenever he would sleep with his brother's wife, he would spill his seed on the ground so that he would not produce offspring for his brother.
**v10** What he did was wicked in the sight of the LORD, so He put Onan to death as well.

**v11** Then Judah said to his daughter-in-law Tamar, "Live as a widow in your father's house until my son Shelah grows up." For he thought, "He may die too, like his brothers." So Tamar went to live in her father's house.

**v12** After a long time Judah's wife, the daughter of Shua, died. When Judah had finished mourning, he and his friend Hirah the Adullamite went up to his sheepshearers at Timnah.
**v13** When Tamar was told, "Your father-in-law is going up to Timnah to shear his sheep,"
**v14** she removed her widow's garments, covered her face with a veil to disguise herself, and sat at the entrance to Enaim, which is on the way to Timnah. For she saw that although Shelah had grown up, she had not been given to him as a wife.

**v15** When Judah saw her, he thought she was a prostitute because she had covered her face.
**v16** Not realizing that she was his daughter-in-law, he went over to her and said, "Come now, let me sleep with you.""What will you give me for sleeping with you?" she inquired.

**v17** "I will send you a young goat from my flock," Judah answered.But she replied, "Only if you leave me something as a pledge until you send it."

**v18** "What pledge should I give you?" he asked.She answered, "Your seal and your cord, and the staff in your hand." So he gave them to her and slept with her, and she became pregnant by him.
**v19** Then Tamar got up and departed. And she removed her veil and put on her widow's garments again.

**v20** Now when Judah sent his friend Hirah the Adullamite with the young goat to collect the items he had left with the woman, he could not find her.
**v21** He asked the men of that place, "Where is the shrine prostitute who was beside the road at Enaim?""No shrine prostitute has been here," they answered.

**v22** So Hirah returned to Judah and said, "I could not find her, and furthermore, the men of that place said, 'No shrine prostitute has been here.'"
