**v2** "Tell the Israelites to bring Me an offering. You are to receive My offering from every man whose heart compels him.
**v3** This is the offering you are to accept from them:gold, silver, and bronze;

**v4** blue, purple, and scarlet yarn; fine linen and goat hair;

**v5** ram skins dyed red and fine leather; [^1] acacia wood;

**v6** olive oil for the light; spices for the anointing oil and for the fragrant incense;

**v7** and onyx stones and gemstones to be mounted on the ephod and breastpiece.

**v8** And they are to make a sanctuary for Me, so that I may dwell among them.
**v9** You must make the tabernacle and design all its furnishings according to the pattern I show you.
#### The Ark of the Covenant

**v10** And they are to construct an ark of acacia wood, two and a half cubits long, a cubit and a half wide, and a cubit and a half high. [^2]
**v11** Overlay it with pure gold both inside and out, and make a gold molding around it.

**v12** Cast four gold rings for it and fasten them to its four feet, two rings on one side and two on the other.
**v13** And make poles of acacia wood and overlay them with gold.
**v14** Insert the poles into the rings on the sides of the ark, in order to carry it.
**v15** The poles are to remain in the rings of the ark; they must not be removed.
**v16** And place inside the ark the Testimony, [^3] which I will give you.
#### The Mercy Seat

**v17** And you are to construct a mercy seat [^4] of pure gold, two and a half cubits long and a cubit and a half wide. [^5]
**v18** Make two cherubim of hammered gold at the ends of the mercy seat,
**v19** one cherub on one end and one on the other, all made from one piece of gold.
**v20** And the cherubim are to have wings that spread upward, overshadowing the mercy seat. The cherubim are to face each other, looking toward the mercy seat.

**v21** Set the mercy seat atop the ark and put the Testimony that I will give you into the ark.

**v22** And I will meet with you there above the mercy seat, between the two cherubim that are over the ark of the Testimony; [^6] I will speak with you about all that I command you regarding the Israelites.
#### The Table of Showbread

**v23** You are also to make a table of acacia wood two cubits long, a cubit wide, and a cubit and a half high. [^7]
**v24** Overlay it with pure gold and make a gold molding around it.
**v25** And make a rim around it a handbreadth wide [^8] and put a gold molding on the rim.

**v26** Make four gold rings for the table and fasten them to the four corners at its four legs.
**v27** The rings are to be close to the rim, to serve as holders for the poles used to carry the table.
**v28** Make the poles of acacia wood and overlay them with gold, so that the table may be carried with them.

**v29** You are also to make the plates and dishes, as well as the pitchers and bowls for pouring drink offerings. Make them out of pure gold.

**v30** And place the Bread of the Presence on the table before Me at all times.
#### The Lampstand

**v31** Then you are to make a lampstand of pure, hammered gold. It shall be made of one piece, including its base and shaft, its cups, and its buds and petals.

**v32** Six branches are to extend from the sides of the lampstand—three on one side and three on the other.
**v33** There are to be three cups shaped like almond blossoms on the first branch, each with buds and petals, three on the next branch, and the same for all six branches that extend from the lampstand.

**v34** And on the lampstand there shall be four cups shaped like almond blossoms with buds and petals.
**v35** For the six branches that extend from the lampstand, a bud must be under the first pair of branches, a bud under the second pair, and a bud under the third pair.
**v36** The buds and branches are to be all of one piece with the lampstand, hammered out of pure gold.

**v37** Make seven lamps and set them up on the lampstand so that they illuminate the area in front of it.
**v38** The wick trimmers and their trays must be of pure gold.
**v39** The lampstand and all these utensils shall be made from a talent of pure gold. [^9]

**v40** See to it that you make everything according to the pattern shown you on the mountain. [^10]
[^1]: Possibly the hides of large aquatic mammals ( 25:5)
[^2]: The ark was approximately 3.75 feet long, 2.25 feet wide, and 2.25 feet high (114.3 centimeters long, 68.6 centimeters wide, and 68.6 centimeters high). ( 25:10)
[^3]: The Testimony refers to the stone tablets in the ark of the covenant inscribed with the Ten Commandments; also in verses 21 and 22. ( 25:16)
[^4]: Or an atonement cover; here and throughout Exodus ( 25:17)
[^5]: The mercy seat was approximately 3.75 feet long and 2.25 feet wide (114.3 centimeters long and 68.6 centimeters wide). ( 25:17)
[^6]: That is, the ark of the covenant ( 25:22)
[^7]: The table was approximately 3 feet long, 1.5 feet wide, and 2.25 feet high (91.4 centimeters long, 45.7 centimeters wide, and 68.6 centimeters high). ( 25:23)
[^8]: A handbreadth is approximately 2.9 inches or 7.4 centimeters. ( 25:25)
[^9]: A talent is approximately 75.4 pounds or 34.2 kilograms of gold. ( 25:39)
[^10]: Cited in Hebrews 8:5 ( 25:40)

### Chapter 26

#### The Ten Curtains for the Tabernacle
**v1** "You are to construct the tabernacle itself with ten curtains of finely spun linen, each with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and cherubim skillfully worked into them.
**v2** Each curtain shall be twenty-eight cubits long and four cubits wide [^1]—all curtains the same size.

**v3** Five of the curtains are to be joined together, and the other five joined as well.
**v4** Make loops of blue material on the edge of the end curtain in the first set, and do the same for the end curtain in the second set.

**v5** Make fifty loops on one curtain and fifty loops on the end curtain of the second set, so that the loops line up opposite one another.
**v6** Make fifty gold clasps as well, and join the curtains together with the clasps, so that the tabernacle will be a unit.
#### The Eleven Curtains of Goat Hair

**v7** You are to make curtains of goat hair for the tent over the tabernacle—eleven curtains in all.
**v8** Each of the eleven curtains is to be the same size—thirty cubits long and four cubits wide. [^2]

**v9** Join five of the curtains into one set and the other six into another. Then fold the sixth curtain over double at the front of the tent.

**v10** Make fifty loops along the edge of the end curtain in the first set, and fifty loops along the edge of the corresponding curtain in the second set.
**v11** Make fifty bronze clasps and put them through the loops to join the tent together as a unit.

**v12** As for the overlap that remains of the tent curtains, the half curtain that is left over shall hang down over the back of the tabernacle.
**v13** And the tent curtains will be a cubit [^3] longer on either side, and the excess will hang over the sides of the tabernacle to cover it.

**v14** Also make a covering for the tent out of ram skins dyed red, and over that a covering of fine leather. [^4]
#### The Frames and Bases

**v15** You are to construct upright frames of acacia wood for the tabernacle.
**v16** Each frame is to be ten cubits long and a cubit and a half wide. [^5]
**v17** Two tenons [^6] must be connected to each other for each frame. Make all the frames of the tabernacle in this way.

**v18** Construct twenty frames for the south side of the tabernacle,
**v19** with forty silver bases under the twenty frames—two bases for each frame, one under each tenon.

**v20** For the second side of the tabernacle, the north side, make twenty frames
**v21** and forty silver bases—two bases under each frame.

**v22** Make six frames for the rear of the tabernacle, the west side,
**v23** and two frames for the two back corners of the tabernacle,
**v24** coupled together from bottom to top and fitted into a single ring. These will serve as the two corners.
**v25** So there are to be eight frames and sixteen silver bases—two under each frame.

**v26** You are also to make five crossbars of acacia wood for the frames on one side of the tabernacle,
**v27** five for those on the other side, and five for those on the rear side of the tabernacle, to the west.

**v28** The central crossbar in the middle of the frames shall extend from one end to the other.
**v29** Overlay the frames with gold and make gold rings to hold the crossbars. Also overlay the crossbars with gold.

**v30** So you are to set up the tabernacle according to the pattern shown you on the mountain.
#### The Veil

**v31** Make a veil of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen, with cherubim skillfully worked into it.
**v32** Hang it with gold hooks on four posts of acacia wood, overlaid with gold and standing on four silver bases.
**v33** And hang the veil from the clasps and place the ark of the Testimony [^7] behind the veil. So the veil will separate the Holy Place from the Most Holy Place. [^8]

**v34** Put the mercy seat on the ark of the Testimony in the Most Holy Place.
**v35** And place the table outside the veil on the north side of the tabernacle, and put the lampstand opposite the table, on the south side.
#### The Curtain for the Entrance

**v36** For the entrance to the tent, you are to make a curtain embroidered with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen.
**v37** Make five posts of acacia wood for the curtain, overlay them with gold hooks, and cast five bronze bases for them.
[^1]: Each of the ten curtains was approximately 42 feet long and 6 feet wide (12.8 meters long and 1.8 meters wide). ( 26:2)
[^2]: Each of the eleven curtains was approximately 45 feet long and 6 feet wide (13.7 meters long and 1.8 meters wide). ( 26:8)
[^3]: A cubit is approximately 18 inches or 45.7 centimeters. ( 26:13)
[^4]: Possibly the hides of large aquatic mammals ( 26:14)
[^5]: Each frame was approximately 15 feet long and 2.25 feet wide (4.6 meters long and 68.6 centimeters wide). ( 26:16)
[^6]: That is, projecting pieces of wood made for insertion into another piece; similarly in verse 19. ( 26:17)
[^7]: That is, the ark of the covenant; also in verse 34 ( 26:33)
[^8]: Or the Holy of Holies; also in verse 34 ( 26:33)

### Chapter 27

#### The Bronze Altar
**v1** "You are to build an altar of acacia wood. The altar must be square, five cubits long, five cubits wide, and three cubits high. [^1]
**v2** Make a horn on each of its four corners, so that the horns are of one piece, and overlay it with bronze.

**v3** Make all its utensils of bronze—its pots for removing ashes, its shovels, its sprinkling bowls, its meat forks, and its firepans.
**v4** Construct for it a grate of bronze mesh, and make a bronze ring at each of the four corners of the mesh.
**v5** Set the grate beneath the ledge of the altar, so that the mesh comes halfway up the altar.

**v6** Additionally, make poles of acacia wood for the altar and overlay them with bronze.
**v7** The poles are to be inserted into the rings so that the poles are on two sides of the altar when it is carried.

**v8** Construct the altar with boards so that it is hollow. It is to be made just as you were shown on the mountain.
#### The Courtyard

**v9** You are also to make a courtyard for the tabernacle. On the south side of the courtyard make curtains of finely spun linen, a hundred cubits long [^2] on one side,
**v10** with twenty posts and twenty bronze bases, and silver hooks and bands on the posts.

**v11** Likewise there are to be curtains on the north side, a hundred cubits long, with twenty posts and twenty bronze bases, and with silver hooks and bands on the posts.
**v12** The curtains on the west side of the courtyard shall be fifty cubits wide, [^3] with ten posts and ten bases.

**v13** The east side of the courtyard, toward the sunrise, is to be fifty cubits wide.
**v14** Make the curtains on one side fifteen cubits long, [^4] with three posts and three bases,
**v15** and the curtains on the other side fifteen cubits long, with three posts and three bases.

**v16** The gate of the courtyard shall be twenty cubits long, [^5] with a curtain embroidered with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen. It shall have four posts and four bases.

**v17** All the posts around the courtyard shall have silver bands, silver hooks, and bronze bases.
**v18** The entire courtyard shall be a hundred cubits long and fifty cubits wide, [^6] with curtains of finely spun linen five cubits high, [^7] and with bronze bases.
**v19** All the utensils of the tabernacle for every use, including all its tent pegs and the tent pegs of the courtyard, shall be made of bronze.
#### The Oil for the Lamps

**v20** And you are to command the Israelites to bring you pure oil of pressed olives for the light, to keep the lamps burning continually.

**v21** In the Tent of Meeting, outside the veil that is in front of the Testimony, [^8] Aaron and his sons are to tend the lamps before the LORD from evening until morning. This is to be a permanent statute for the Israelites for the generations to come.
[^1]: The altar was approximately 7.5 feet in length and width, and 4.5 feet high (2.3 meters in length and width, and 1.4 meters high). ( 27:1)
[^2]: 100 cubits is approximately 150 feet or 45.7 meters; also in verse 11. ( 27:9)
[^3]: 50 cubits is approximately 75 feet or 22.9 meters; also in verse 13. ( 27:12)
[^4]: 15 cubits is approximately 22.5 feet or 6.9 meters; also in verse 15. ( 27:14)
[^5]: 20 cubits is approximately 30 feet or 9.1 meters. ( 27:16)
[^6]: The courtyard was approximately 150 feet long and 75 feet wide (45.7 meters long and 22.9 meters wide). ( 27:18)
[^7]: 5 cubits is approximately 7.5 feet or 2.3 meters. ( 27:18)
[^8]: The Testimony refers to the stone tablets in the ark of the covenant inscribed with the Ten Commandments. ( 27:21)

### Chapter 28

#### Garments for the Priests
**v1** "Next, have your brother Aaron brought to you from among the Israelites, along with his sons Nadab, Abihu, Eleazar, and Ithamar, to serve Me as priests.
**v2** Make holy garments for your brother Aaron, to give him glory and splendor.

**v3** You are to instruct all the skilled craftsmen, whom I have filled with a spirit of wisdom, to make garments for Aaron's consecration, so that he may serve Me as priest.
**v4** These are the garments that they shall make: a breastpiece, an ephod, a robe, a woven tunic, a turban, and a sash. They are to make these holy garments for your brother Aaron and his sons, so that they may serve Me as priests.
**v5** They shall use gold, along with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and fine linen.
#### The Ephod

**v6** They are to make the ephod of finely spun linen embroidered with gold, and with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn.
**v7** It shall have two shoulder pieces attached at two of its corners, so it can be fastened.
**v8** And the skillfully woven waistband of the ephod must be of one piece, of the same workmanship—with gold, with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and with finely spun linen.

**v9** Take two onyx stones and engrave on them the names of the sons of Israel:
**v10** six of their names on one stone and the remaining six on the other, in the order of their birth.
**v11** Engrave the names of the sons of Israel on the two stones the way a gem cutter engraves a seal. Then mount the stones in gold filigree settings.
**v12** Fasten both stones on the shoulder pieces of the ephod as memorial stones for the sons of Israel. Aaron is to bear their names on his two shoulders as a memorial before the LORD.

**v13** Fashion gold filigree settings
**v14** and two chains of pure gold, made of braided cord work; and attach these chains to the settings.
#### The Breastpiece

**v15** You are also to make a breastpiece of judgment with the same workmanship as the ephod. Construct it with gold, with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and with finely spun linen.
**v16** It must be square when folded over double, a span long and a span wide. [^1]

**v17** And mount on it a setting of gemstones, four rows of stones: [^2] In the first row there shall be a ruby, a topaz, and an emerald;

**v18** in the second row a turquoise, a sapphire, and a diamond;

**v19** in the third row a jacinth, an agate, and an amethyst;

**v20** and in the fourth row a beryl, an onyx, and a jasper.Mount these stones in gold filigree settings.
**v21** The twelve stones are to correspond to the names of the sons of Israel, each engraved like a seal with the name of one of the twelve tribes.

**v22** For the breastpiece, make braided chains like cords of pure gold.
**v23** You are also to make two gold rings and fasten them to the two corners of the breastpiece.
**v24** Then fasten the two gold chains to the two gold rings at the corners of the breastpiece,
**v25** and fasten the other ends of the two chains to the two filigree settings, attaching them to the shoulder pieces of the ephod at the front.

**v26** Make two more gold rings and attach them to the other two corners of the breastpiece, on the inside edge next to the ephod.

**v27** Make two additional gold rings and attach them to the bottom of the two shoulder pieces of the ephod, on its front, near its seam just above its woven waistband.
**v28** The rings of the breastpiece shall be tied to the rings of the ephod with a cord of blue yarn, so that the breastpiece is above the waistband of the ephod and does not swing out from the ephod.

**v29** Whenever Aaron enters the Holy Place, he shall bear the names of the sons of Israel over his heart on the breastpiece of judgment, as a continual reminder before the LORD.

**v30** And place the Urim and Thummim [^3] in the breastpiece of judgment, so that they will also be over Aaron's heart whenever he comes before the LORD. Aaron will continually carry the judgment of the sons of Israel over his heart before the LORD.
#### Additional Priestly Garments

**v31** You are to make the robe of the ephod entirely of blue cloth,
**v32** with an opening at its top in the center. Around the opening shall be a woven collar with an opening like that of a garment, [^4] so that it will not tear.

**v33** Make pomegranates of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn all the way around the lower hem, with gold bells between them,
**v34** alternating the gold bells and pomegranates around the lower hem of the robe.

**v35** Aaron must wear the robe whenever he ministers, and its sound will be heard when he enters or exits the sanctuary before the LORD, so that he will not die.

**v36** You are to make a plate of pure gold and engrave on it as on a seal:HOLY TO THE LORD. [^5]

**v37** Fasten to it a blue cord to mount it on the turban; it shall be on the front of the turban.
**v38** And it will be worn on Aaron's forehead, so that he may bear the iniquity of the holy things that the sons of Israel consecrate with regard to all their holy gifts. It shall always be on his forehead, so that they may be acceptable before the LORD.

**v39** You are to weave the tunic with fine linen, make the turban of fine linen, and fashion an embroidered sash.
**v40** Make tunics, sashes, and headbands for Aaron's sons, to give them glory and splendor.

**v41** After you put these garments on your brother Aaron and his sons, anoint them, ordain them, and consecrate them so that they may serve Me as priests.

**v42** Make linen undergarments to cover their bare flesh, extending from waist to thigh.
**v43** Aaron and his sons must wear them whenever they enter the Tent of Meeting or approach the altar to minister in the Holy Place, so that they will not incur guilt and die. This is to be a permanent statute for Aaron and his descendants.
[^1]: The breastpiece, when folded over, was approximately 9 inches or 22.9 centimeters in both length and width. ( 28:16)
[^2]: The precise identification of some of these gemstones is uncertain. ( 28:17)
[^3]: Literally Lights and Perfections ( 28:30)
[^4]: The meaning of the Hebrew word is uncertain; possibly a coat of mail. ( 28:32)
[^5]: That is, the LORD ( 28:36)

### Chapter 29

#### Consecration of the Priests
**v1** "Now this is what you are to do to consecrate Aaron and his sons to serve Me as priests: Take a young bull and two rams without blemish,
**v2** along with unleavened bread, unleavened cakes mixed with oil, and unleavened wafers anointed with oil. Make them out of fine wheat flour,
**v3** put them in a basket, and present them in the basket, along with the bull and the two rams.

**v4** Then present Aaron and his sons at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting and wash them with water.
**v5** Take the garments and clothe Aaron with the tunic, the robe of the ephod, the ephod itself, and the breastplate. Fasten the ephod on him with its woven waistband.
**v6** Put the turban on his head and attach the holy diadem to the turban.
**v7** Then take the anointing oil and anoint him by pouring it on his head.

**v8** Present his sons as well and clothe them with tunics.
**v9** Wrap the sashes around Aaron and his sons and tie headbands on them. The priesthood shall be theirs by a permanent statute. In this way you are to ordain Aaron and his sons.
#### The Order of the Sacrifices

**v10** You are to present the bull at the front of the Tent of Meeting, and Aaron and his sons are to lay their hands on its head.
**v11** And you shall slaughter the bull before the LORD at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting.
**v12** Take some of the blood of the bull and put it on the horns of the altar with your finger; then pour out the rest of the blood at the base of the altar.
**v13** Take all the fat that covers the entrails and the lobe of the liver, and both kidneys with the fat on them, and burn them on the altar.
**v14** But burn the flesh of the bull and its hide and dung outside the camp; it is a sin offering. [^1]

**v15** Take one of the rams, and Aaron and his sons shall lay their hands on its head.
**v16** You are to slaughter the ram, take its blood, and splatter it on all sides of the altar.
**v17** Cut the ram into pieces, wash the entrails and legs, and place them with its head and other pieces.
**v18** Then burn the entire ram on the altar; it is a burnt offering to the LORD, a pleasing aroma, a food offering to the LORD.

**v19** Take the second ram, and Aaron and his sons are to lay their hands on its head.
**v20** Slaughter the ram, take some of its blood, and put it on the right earlobes of Aaron and his sons, on the thumbs of their right hands, and on the big toes of their right feet. Splatter the remaining blood on all sides of the altar.
**v21** And take some of the blood on the altar and some of the anointing oil and sprinkle it on Aaron and his garments, as well as on his sons and their garments. Then he and his garments will be consecrated, as well as his sons and their garments.

**v22** Take the fat from the ram, the fat tail, the fat covering the entrails, the lobe of the liver, both kidneys with the fat on them, and the right thigh (since this is a ram for ordination),
**v23** along with one loaf of bread, one cake of bread made with oil, and one wafer from the basket of unleavened bread that is before the LORD.
**v24** Put all these in the hands of Aaron and his sons and wave them before the LORD as a wave offering.
**v25** Then take them from their hands and burn them on the altar atop the burnt offering as a pleasing aroma before the LORD; it is a food offering to the LORD.

**v26** Take the breast of the ram of Aaron's ordination and wave it before the LORD as a wave offering, and it will be your portion.
**v27** Consecrate for Aaron and his sons the breast of the wave offering that is waved and the thigh of the heave offering that is lifted up from the ram of ordination.
**v28** This will belong to Aaron and his sons as a regular portion from the Israelites, for it is the heave offering the Israelites will make to the LORD from their peace offerings.

**v29** The holy garments that belong to Aaron will belong to his sons after him, so they can be anointed and ordained in them.
**v30** The son who succeeds him as priest and enters the Tent of Meeting to minister in the Holy Place must wear them for seven days.
#### Food for the Priests

**v31** You are to take the ram of ordination and boil its flesh in a holy place.
**v32** At the entrance to the Tent of Meeting, Aaron and his sons are to eat the meat of the ram and the bread that is in the basket.
**v33** They must eat those things by which atonement was made for their ordination and consecration. But no outsider may eat them, because these things are sacred.
**v34** And if any of the meat of ordination or any bread is left until the morning, you are to burn up the remainder. It must not be eaten, because it is sacred.

**v35** This is what you are to do for Aaron and his sons based on all that I have commanded you, taking seven days to ordain them.
**v36** Sacrifice a bull as a sin offering each day for atonement. Purify the altar by making atonement for it, and anoint it to consecrate it.
**v37** For seven days you shall make atonement for the altar and consecrate it. Then the altar will become most holy; whatever touches the altar will be holy.
#### The Daily Offerings

**v38** This is what you are to offer regularly on the altar, each day: two lambs that are a year old.
**v39** Offer one lamb in the morning and the other at twilight. [^2]
**v40** With the first lamb offer a tenth of an ephah of fine flour, [^3] mixed with a quarter hin of oil from pressed olives, [^4] and a drink offering of a quarter hin of wine.
**v41** And offer the second lamb at twilight with the same grain offering and drink offering as in the morning, as a pleasing aroma, a food offering to the LORD.

**v42** For the generations to come, this burnt offering shall be made regularly at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting before the LORD, where I will meet you to speak with you.
**v43** I will also meet with the Israelites there, and that place will be consecrated by My glory.
**v44** So I will consecrate the Tent of Meeting and the altar, and I will consecrate Aaron and his sons to serve Me as priests.
#### God Will Dwell among the People

**v45** Then I will dwell among the Israelites and be their God.
**v46** And they will know that I am the LORD their God, who brought them out of the land of Egypt so that I might dwell among them.I am the LORD their God.
[^1]: Or purification offering; also in verse 36 ( 29:14)
[^2]: Hebrew between the two evenings; also in verse 41 ( 29:39)
[^3]: A tenth of an ephah is approximately 2 dry quarts or 2.2 liters (probably about 2.6 pounds or 1.2 kilograms of flour). ( 29:40)
[^4]: Hebrew a quarter hin of pressed oil; that is, approximately 0.97 quarts or 0.92 liters ( 29:40)

### Chapter 30

#### The Altar of Incense
**v1** "You are also to make an altar of acacia wood for the burning of incense.
**v2** It is to be square, a cubit long, a cubit wide, and two cubits high. [^1] Its horns must be of one piece.
**v3** Overlay with pure gold the top and all the sides and horns, and make a molding of gold around it.
**v4** And make two gold rings below the molding on opposite sides to hold the poles used to carry it.
**v5** Make the poles of acacia wood and overlay them with gold.

**v6** Place the altar in front of the veil that is before the ark of the Testimony [^2]—before the mercy seat that is over the Testimony—where I will meet with you.
**v7** And Aaron is to burn fragrant incense on it every morning when he tends the lamps.
**v8** When Aaron sets up the lamps at twilight, [^3] he must burn the incense perpetually before the LORD for the generations to come.
**v9** On this altar you must not offer unauthorized [^4] incense or a burnt offering or grain offering; nor are you to pour a drink offering on it.

**v10** Once a year Aaron shall make atonement on the horns of the altar. Throughout your generations he shall make atonement on it annually with the blood of the sin offering [^5] of atonement. The altar is most holy to the LORD."
#### The Census Offering

**v11** Then the LORD said to Moses,
**v12** "When you take a census of the Israelites to number them, each man must pay the LORD a ransom for his life when he is counted. Then no plague will come upon them when they are numbered.
**v13** Everyone who crosses over to those counted must pay a half shekel, [^6] according to the sanctuary shekel, which weighs twenty gerahs. [^7] This half shekel is an offering to the LORD.

**v14** Everyone twenty years of age or older who crosses over must give this offering to the LORD.
**v15** In making the offering to the LORD to atone for your lives, the rich shall not give more than a half shekel, nor shall the poor give less.
**v16** Take the atonement money from the Israelites and use it for the service of the Tent of Meeting. It will serve as a memorial for the Israelites before the LORD to make atonement for your lives."
#### The Bronze Basin

**v17** And the LORD said to Moses,
**v18** "You are to make a bronze basin with a bronze stand for washing. Set it between the Tent of Meeting and the altar, and put water in it,
**v19** with which Aaron and his sons are to wash their hands and feet.
**v20** Whenever they enter the Tent of Meeting or approach the altar to minister by presenting a food offering to the LORD, they must wash with water so that they will not die.
**v21** Thus they are to wash their hands and feet so that they will not die; this shall be a permanent statute for Aaron and his descendants for the generations to come."
#### The Anointing Oil

**v22** Then the LORD said to Moses,
**v23** "Take the finest spices: 500 shekels of liquid myrrh, [^8] half that amount (250 shekels) of fragrant cinnamon, [^9]250 shekels of fragrant cane, [^10]
**v24** 500 shekels of cassia [^11]—all according to the sanctuary shekel—and a hin of olive oil. [^12]
**v25** Prepare from these a sacred anointing oil, a fragrant blend, the work of a perfumer; it will be a sacred anointing oil.

**v26** Use this oil to anoint the Tent of Meeting, the ark of the Testimony,
**v27** the table and all its utensils, the lampstand and its utensils, the altar of incense,
**v28** the altar of burnt offering and all its utensils, and the basin with its stand.
**v29** You are to consecrate them so that they will be most holy. Whatever touches them shall be holy.
**v30** Anoint Aaron and his sons and consecrate them to serve Me as priests.

**v31** And you are to tell the Israelites, 'This will be My sacred anointing oil for the generations to come.
**v32** It must not be used to anoint an ordinary man, and you must not make anything like it with the same formula. It is holy, and it must be holy to you.
**v33** Anyone who mixes perfume like it or puts it on an outsider shall be cut off from his people.'"
#### The Incense

**v34** The LORD also said to Moses, "Take fragrant spices—gum resin, onycha, galbanum, and pure frankincense—in equal measures,
**v35** and make a fragrant blend of incense, the work of a perfumer, seasoned with salt, pure and holy.
**v36** Grind some of it into fine powder and place it in front of the Testimony [^13] in the Tent of Meeting, where I will meet with you. It shall be most holy to you.
**v37** You are never to use this formula to make incense for yourselves; you shall regard it as holy to the LORD.
**v38** Anyone who makes something like it to enjoy its fragrance shall be cut off from his people."
[^1]: The altar was approximately 1.5 feet in length and width, and 3 feet high (45.7 centimeters in length and width, and 91.4 centimeters high). ( 30:2)
[^2]: That is, the ark of the covenant; also in verse 26 ( 30:6)
[^3]: Hebrew between the two evenings ( 30:8)
[^4]: Or strange ( 30:9)
[^5]: Or purification offering ( 30:10)
[^6]: A half shekel is approximately 0.2 ounces or 5.7 grams; also in verse 15. ( 30:13)
[^7]: 20 gerahs is equivalent to one shekel (approximately 0.4 ounces or 11.4 grams). ( 30:13)
[^8]: 500 shekels is approximately 12.6 pounds or 5.7 kilograms of myrrh. ( 30:23)
[^9]: 250 shekels is approximately 6.3 pounds or 2.9 kilograms of cinnamon. ( 30:23)
[^10]: 250 shekels is approximately 6.3 pounds or 2.9 kilograms of cane. ( 30:23)
[^11]: 500 shekels is approximately 12.6 pounds or 5.7 kilograms of cassia. ( 30:24)
[^12]: A hin is approximately 0.97 gallons or 3.67 liters of olive oil. ( 30:24)
[^13]: The Testimony refers to the stone tablets in the ark of the covenant inscribed with the Ten Commandments. ( 30:36)

### Chapter 31

#### Bezalel and Oholiab
**v1** Then the LORD said to Moses,
**v2** "See, I have called by name Bezalel son of Uri, the son of Hur, of the tribe of Judah.
**v3** And I have filled him with the Spirit of God, with skill, ability, and knowledge in all kinds of craftsmanship,
**v4** to design artistic works in gold, silver, and bronze,
**v5** to cut gemstones for settings, and to carve wood, so that he may be a master of every craft.

**v6** Moreover, I have selected Oholiab son of Ahisamach, of the tribe of Dan, as his assistant.I have also given skill to all the craftsmen, that they may fashion all that I have commanded you:
**v7** the Tent of Meeting, the ark of the Testimony [^1] and the mercy seat upon it, and all the other furnishings of the tent—
**v8** the table with its utensils, the pure gold lampstand with all its utensils, the altar of incense,
**v9** the altar of burnt offering with all its utensils, and the basin with its stand—
**v10** as well as the woven garments, both the holy garments for Aaron the priest and the garments for his sons to serve as priests,
**v11** in addition to the anointing oil and fragrant incense for the Holy Place. They are to make them according to all that I have commanded you."
#### The Sign of the Sabbath

**v12** And the LORD said to Moses,
**v13** "Tell the Israelites, 'Surely you must keep My Sabbaths, for this will be a sign between Me and you for the generations to come, so that you may know that I am the LORD who sanctifies you.
**v14** Keep the Sabbath, for it is holy to you. Anyone who profanes it must surely be put to death. Whoever does any work on that day must be cut off from among his people.
**v15** For six days work may be done, but the seventh day is a Sabbath of complete rest, holy to the LORD. Whoever does any work on the Sabbath day must surely be put to death.

**v16** The Israelites must keep the Sabbath, celebrating it as a permanent covenant for the generations to come.
**v17** It is a sign between Me and the Israelites forever; for in six days the LORD made the heavens and the earth, but on the seventh day He rested and was refreshed.'"
#### Moses Receives the Tablets

**v18** When the LORD had finished speaking with Moses on Mount Sinai, He gave him the two tablets of the Testimony, tablets of stone inscribed by the finger of God.
[^1]: That is, the ark of the covenant ( 31:7)

### Chapter 32

#### The Golden Calf
**v1** Now when the people saw that Moses was delayed in coming down from the mountain, they gathered around Aaron and said, "Come, make us gods who will go before us. As for this Moses who brought us up out of the land of Egypt, we do not know what has happened to him!"[^1]

**v2** So Aaron told them, "Take off the gold earrings that are on your wives and sons and daughters, and bring them to me."

**v3** Then all the people took off their gold earrings and brought them to Aaron.
**v4** He took the gold from their hands, and with an engraving tool he fashioned it into a molten calf. And they said, "These, O Israel, are your gods, who brought you up out of the land of Egypt!"

**v5** When Aaron saw this, he built an altar before the calf and proclaimed: "Tomorrow shall be a feast to the LORD."

**v6** So the next day they arose, offered burnt offerings, and presented peace offerings. And the people sat down to eat and drink and got up to indulge in revelry. [^2]

**v7** Then the LORD said to Moses, "Go down at once, for your people, whom you brought up out of the land of Egypt, have corrupted themselves.
**v8** How quickly they have turned aside from the way that I commanded them! They have made for themselves a molten calf and have bowed down to it. They have sacrificed to it and said, 'These, O Israel, are your gods, who brought you up out of the land of Egypt.'"

**v9** The LORD also said to Moses, "I have seen this people, and they are indeed a stiff-necked people.
**v10** Now leave Me alone, so that My anger may burn against them and consume them. Then I will make you into a great nation."

**v11** But Moses sought the favor of the LORD his God, saying, "O LORD, why does Your anger burn against Your people, whom You brought out of the land of Egypt with great power and a mighty hand?
**v12** Why should the Egyptians declare, 'He brought them out with evil intent, to kill them in the mountains and wipe them from the face of the earth'? Turn from Your fierce anger and relent from doing harm to Your people.
**v13** Remember Your servants Abraham, Isaac, and Israel, to whom You swore by Your very self when You declared, 'I will make your descendants as numerous as the stars in the sky, and I will give your descendants all this land that I have promised, and it shall be their inheritance forever.'"

**v14** So the LORD relented from the calamity He had threatened to bring on His people.

**v15** Then Moses turned and went down the mountain with the two tablets of the Testimony in his hands. They were inscribed on both sides, front and back.
**v16** The tablets were the work of God, and the writing was the writing of God, engraved on the tablets.

**v17** When Joshua heard the sound of the people shouting, he said to Moses, "The sound of war is in the camp."

**v18** But Moses replied: "It is neither the cry of victory nor the cry of defeat; I hear the sound of singing!"

**v19** As Moses approached the camp and saw the calf and the dancing, he burned with anger and threw the tablets out of his hands, shattering them at the base of the mountain.
**v20** Then he took the calf they had made, burned it in the fire, ground it to powder, and scattered the powder over the face of the water. Then he forced the Israelites to drink it.

**v21** "What did this people do to you," Moses asked Aaron, "that you have led them into so great a sin?"

**v22** "Do not be enraged, my lord," Aaron replied. "You yourself know that the people are intent on evil.
**v23** They told me, 'Make us gods who will go before us. As for this Moses who brought us up out of the land of Egypt, we do not know what has happened to him!'

**v24** So I said to them, 'Whoever has gold, let him take it off,' and they gave it to me. And when I threw it into the fire, out came this calf!"

**v25** Moses saw that the people were out of control, for Aaron had let them run wild and become a laughingstock [^3] to their enemies.
**v26** So Moses stood at the entrance to the camp and said, "Whoever is for the LORD, come to me." And all the Levites gathered around him.

**v27** He told them, "This is what the LORD, the God of Israel, says: 'Each of you men is to fasten his sword to his side, go back and forth through the camp from gate to gate, and slay his brother, his friend, and his neighbor.'"

**v28** The Levites did as Moses commanded, and that day about three thousand of the people fell dead.

**v29** Afterward, Moses said, "Today you have been ordained [^4] for service to the LORD, since each man went against his son and his brother; so the LORD has bestowed a blessing on you this day."

**v30** The next day Moses said to the people, "You have committed a great sin. Now I will go up to the LORD; perhaps I can make atonement for your sin."

**v31** So Moses returned to the LORD and said, "Oh, what a great sin these people have committed! They have made gods of gold for themselves.
**v32** Yet now, if You would only forgive their sin.... But if not, please blot me out of the book that You have written."

**v33** The LORD replied to Moses, "Whoever has sinned against Me, I will blot out of My book.
**v34** Now go, lead the people to the place I described. Behold, My angel shall go before you. But on the day I settle accounts, I will punish them for their sin."

**v35** And the LORD sent a plague on the people because of what they had done with the calf that Aaron had made.
[^1]: Cited in Acts 7:40 ( 32:1)
[^2]: Or to play; cited in 1 Corinthians 10:7 ( 32:6)
[^3]: Or and become an object of derision ( 32:25)
[^4]: Or have ordained yourselves ( 32:29)

### Chapter 33

#### The Command to Leave Sinai
**v1** Then the LORD said to Moses, "Leave this place, you and the people you brought up out of the land of Egypt, and go to the land that I promised to Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob when I said, 'I will give it to your descendants.'
**v2** And I will send an angel before you, and I will drive out the Canaanites, Amorites, Hittites, Perizzites, Hivites, and Jebusites.
**v3** Go up to a land flowing with milk and honey. But I will not go with you, because you are a stiff-necked people; otherwise, I might destroy you on the way."

**v4** When the people heard this bad news, they went into mourning, and no one put on any of his jewelry.
**v5** For the LORD had said to Moses, "Tell the Israelites, 'You are a stiff-necked people. If I should go with you for a single moment, I would destroy you. Now take off your jewelry, and I will decide what to do with you.'"

**v6** So the Israelites stripped themselves of their jewelry from Mount Horeb onward. [^1]
#### The Tent of Meeting

**v7** Now Moses used to take the tent and pitch it at a distance outside the camp. He called it the Tent of Meeting, and anyone inquiring of the LORD would go to the Tent of Meeting outside the camp.
**v8** Then, whenever Moses went out to the tent, all the people would stand at the entrances to their own tents and watch Moses until he entered the tent.
**v9** As Moses entered the tent, the pillar of cloud would come down and remain at the entrance, and the LORD would speak with Moses.
**v10** When all the people saw the pillar of cloud standing at the entrance to the tent, they would stand up and worship, each one at the entrance to his own tent.

**v11** Thus the LORD would speak to Moses face to face, as a man speaks to his friend. Then Moses would return to the camp, but his young assistant Joshua son of Nun would not leave the tent.
#### The Promise of God's Presence

**v12** Then Moses said to the LORD, "Look, You have been telling me, 'Lead this people up,' but You have not let me know whom You will send with me. Yet You have said, 'I know you by name, and you have found favor in My sight.'
**v13** Now if indeed I have found favor in Your sight, please let me know Your ways, that I may know You and find favor in Your sight. Remember that this nation is Your people."

**v14** And the LORD answered, "My Presence will go with you, and I will give you rest."

**v15** "If Your Presence does not go with us," Moses replied, "do not lead us up from here.
**v16** For how then can it be known that Your people and I have found favor in Your sight, unless You go with us? How else will we be distinguished from all the other people on the face of the earth?"

**v17** So the LORD said to Moses, "I will do this very thing you have asked, for you have found favor in My sight, and I know you by name."

**v18** Then Moses said, "Please show me Your glory."

**v19** "I will cause all My goodness to pass before you," the LORD replied, "and I will proclaim My name—the LORD—in your presence. I will have mercy on whom I have mercy, and I will have compassion on whom I have compassion."[^2]

**v20** But He added, "You cannot see My face, for no one can see Me and live."

**v21** The LORD continued, "There is a place near Me where you are to stand upon a rock,
**v22** and when My glory passes by, I will put you in a cleft of the rock and cover you with My hand until I have passed by.
**v23** Then I will take My hand away, and you will see My back; but My face must not be seen."
[^1]: That is, from Mount Sinai onward, or possibly a mountain in the range containing Mount Sinai ( 33:6)
[^2]: Cited in Romans 9:15 ( 33:19)

### Chapter 34

#### New Stone Tablets
**v1** Then the LORD said to Moses, "Chisel out two stone tablets like the originals, and I will write on them the words that were on the first tablets, which you broke.
**v2** Be ready in the morning, and come up on Mount Sinai to present yourself before Me on the mountaintop.
**v3** No one may go up with you; in fact, no one may be seen anywhere on the mountain—not even the flocks or herds may graze in front of the mountain."

**v4** So Moses chiseled out two stone tablets like the originals. He rose early in the morning, and taking the two stone tablets in his hands, he went up Mount Sinai as the LORD had commanded him.

**v5** And the LORD descended in a cloud, stood with him there, and proclaimed His name, the LORD.
**v6** Then the LORD passed in front of Moses and called out: "The LORD, the LORD God, is compassionate and gracious, slow to anger, abounding in loving devotion and faithfulness,
**v7** maintaining loving devotion to a thousand generations, [^1] forgiving iniquity, transgression, and sin.Yet He will by no means leave the guilty unpunished; He will visit the iniquity of the fatherson their children and grandchildrento the third and fourth generations."

**v8** Moses immediately bowed down to the ground and worshiped.
**v9** "O Lord," he said, "if I have indeed found favor in Your sight, my Lord, please go with us. Although this is a stiff-necked people, forgive our iniquity and sin, and take us as Your inheritance."
#### The LORD Renews the Covenant

**v10** And the LORD said, "Behold, I am making a covenant. Before all your people I will perform wonders that have never been done in any nation in all the world. All the people among whom you live will see the LORD's work, for it is an awesome thing that I am doing with you.

**v11** Observe what I command you this day. I will drive out before you the Amorites, Canaanites, Hittites, Perizzites, Hivites, and Jebusites.
**v12** Be careful not to make a treaty [^2] with the inhabitants of the land you are entering, lest they become a snare in your midst.
**v13** Rather, you must tear down their altars, smash their sacred stones, and chop down their Asherah poles.
**v14** For you must not worship any other god, for the LORD, whose name is Jealous, is a jealous God.

**v15** Do not make a covenant with the inhabitants of the land, for when they prostitute themselves to their gods and sacrifice to them, they will invite you, and you will eat their sacrifices.
**v16** And when you take some of their daughters as brides for your sons, their daughters will prostitute themselves to their gods and cause your sons to do the same.

**v17** You shall make no molten gods for yourselves.

**v18** You are to keep the Feast of Unleavened Bread. [^3] For seven days at the appointed time in the month of Abib, [^4] you are to eat unleavened bread as I commanded you. For in the month of Abib you came out of Egypt.

**v19** The first offspring of every womb belongs to Me, including all the firstborn males among your livestock, whether cattle or sheep.
**v20** You must redeem the firstborn of a donkey with a lamb; but if you do not redeem it, you are to break its neck. You must redeem all the firstborn of your sons. No one shall appear before Me empty-handed.

**v21** Six days you shall labor, but on the seventh day you shall rest; even in the seasons of plowing and harvesting, you must rest.

**v22** And you are to celebrate the Feast of Weeks [^5] with the firstfruits of the wheat harvest, and the Feast of Ingathering [^6] at the turn of the year.
**v23** Three times a year all your males are to appear before the Lord GOD, the God of Israel.
**v24** For I will drive out the nations before you and enlarge your borders, and no one will covet your land when you go up three times a year to appear before the LORD your God.

**v25** Do not offer the blood of a sacrifice to Me along with anything leavened, and do not let any of the sacrifice from the Passover Feast remain until morning.

**v26** Bring the best of the firstfruits of your soil to the house of the LORD your God.You must not cook a young goat in its mother's milk."

**v27** The LORD also said to Moses, "Write down these words, for in accordance with these words I have made a covenant with you and with Israel."

**v28** So Moses was there with the LORD forty days and forty nights without eating bread or drinking water. He wrote on the tablets the words of the covenant—the Ten Commandments. [^7]

**v29** And when Moses came down from Mount Sinai with the two tablets of the Testimony in his hands, he was unaware that his face had become radiant from speaking with the LORD.
**v30** Aaron and all the Israelites looked at Moses, and behold, his face was radiant. And they were afraid to approach him.

**v31** But Moses called out to them; so Aaron and all the leaders of the congregation returned to him, and Moses spoke to them.
**v32** And after this all the Israelites came near, and Moses commanded them to do everything that the LORD had told him on Mount Sinai.

**v33** When Moses had finished speaking with them, he put a veil over his face.
**v34** But whenever Moses went in before the LORD to speak with Him, he would remove the veil until he came out. And when he came out, he would tell the Israelites what he had been commanded,
**v35** and the Israelites would see that the face of Moses was radiant. So Moses would put the veil back over his face until he went in to speak with the LORD.
[^1]: Hebrew to thousands ( 34:7)
[^2]: Forms of the Hebrew berit are translated in most passages as covenant. ( 34:12)
[^3]: That is, the seven-day period after the Passover during which no leaven may be eaten; see Exodus 12:14–20. ( 34:18)
[^4]: Abib was the first month of the ancient Hebrew lunar calendar, usually occurring within the months of March and April; twice in this verse. ( 34:18)
[^5]: That is, Shavuot, the late spring feast of pilgrimage to Jerusalem; it is also known as the Feast of Harvest (see Exodus 23:16) or the Feast of Pentecost (see Acts 2:1). ( 34:22)
[^6]: That is, Sukkot, the autumn feast of pilgrimage to Jerusalem; it is later called the Feast of Tabernacles (or Booths or Shelters). ( 34:22)
[^7]: Hebrew the Ten Words ( 34:28)

### Chapter 35

#### The Sabbath
**v1** Then Moses assembled the whole congregation of Israel and said to them, "These are the things that the LORD has commanded you to do:
**v2** For six days work may be done, but the seventh day shall be your holy day, a Sabbath of complete rest to the LORD. Whoever does any work on that day must be put to death.
**v3** Do not light a fire in any of your dwellings on the Sabbath day."
#### Offerings for the Tabernacle

**v4** Moses also told the whole congregation of Israel, "This is what the LORD has commanded:
**v5** Take from among you an offering to the LORD. Let everyone whose heart is willing bring an offering to the LORD:gold, silver, and bronze;

**v6** blue, purple, and scarlet yarn; fine linen and goat hair;

**v7** ram skins dyed red and fine leather; [^1] acacia wood;

**v8** olive oil for the light; spices for the anointing oil and for the fragrant incense;

**v9** and onyx stones and gemstones to be mounted on the ephod and breastpiece.
#### The Skilled Craftsmen

**v10** Let every skilled craftsman among you come and make everything that the LORD has commanded:

**v11** the tabernacle with its tent and covering, its clasps and frames, its crossbars, posts, and bases;

**v12** the ark with its poles and mercy seat, and the veil to shield it;

**v13** the table with its poles, all its utensils, and the Bread of the Presence;

**v14** the lampstand for light with its accessories and lamps and oil for the light;

**v15** the altar of incense with its poles; the anointing oil and fragrant incense; the curtain for the doorway at the entrance to the tabernacle;

**v16** the altar of burnt offering with its bronze grate, its poles, and all its utensils; the basin with its stand;

**v17** the curtains of the courtyard with its posts and bases, and the curtain for the gate of the courtyard;

**v18** the tent pegs for the tabernacle and for the courtyard, along with their ropes;

**v19** and the woven garments for ministering in the holy place—both the holy garments for Aaron the priest and the garments for his sons to serve as priests."
#### The People Offer Gifts

**v20** Then the whole congregation of Israel withdrew from the presence of Moses.
**v21** And everyone whose heart stirred him and whose spirit prompted him came and brought an offering to the LORD for the work on the Tent of Meeting, for all its services, and for the holy garments.

**v22** So all who had willing hearts, both men and women, came and brought brooches and earrings, rings and necklaces, and all kinds of gold jewelry. And they all presented their gold as a wave offering to the LORD.

**v23** Everyone who had blue, purple, or scarlet yarn, or fine linen, goat hair, ram skins dyed red, or articles of fine leather, brought them.
**v24** And all who could present an offering of silver or bronze brought it as a contribution to the LORD. Also, everyone who had acacia wood for any part of the service brought it.

**v25** Every skilled woman spun with her hands and brought what she had spun: blue, purple, or scarlet yarn, or fine linen.
**v26** And all the skilled women whose hearts were stirred spun the goat hair.

**v27** The leaders brought onyx stones and gemstones to mount on the ephod and breastpiece,
**v28** as well as spices and olive oil for the light, for the anointing oil, and for the fragrant incense.

**v29** So all the men and women of the Israelites whose hearts prompted them brought a freewill offering to the LORD for all the work that the LORD through Moses had commanded them to do.
#### Bezalel and Oholiab

**v30** Then Moses said to the Israelites, "See, the LORD has called by name Bezalel son of Uri, the son of Hur, of the tribe of Judah.
**v31** And He has filled him with the Spirit of God, with skill, ability, and knowledge in all kinds of craftsmanship,
**v32** to design artistic works in gold, silver, and bronze,
**v33** to cut gemstones for settings, and to carve wood, so that he may be a master of every artistic craft.

**v34** And the LORD has given both him and Oholiab son of Ahisamach, of the tribe of Dan, the ability to teach others.
**v35** He has filled them with skill to do all kinds of work as engravers, designers, embroiderers in blue, purple, and scarlet yarn and fine linen, and as weavers—as artistic designers of every kind of craft.
[^1]: Possibly the hides of large aquatic mammals; also in verse 23 ( 35:7)

### Chapter 36

#### The People Bring More than Enough
**v1** "So Bezalel, Oholiab, and every skilled person are to carry out everything commanded by the LORD, who has given them skill and ability to know how to perform all the work of constructing the sanctuary."

**v2** Then Moses summoned Bezalel, Oholiab, and every skilled person whom the LORD had gifted—everyone whose heart stirred him to come and do the work.
**v3** They received from Moses all the contributions that the Israelites had brought to carry out the service of constructing the sanctuary.Meanwhile, the people continued to bring freewill offerings morning after morning,
**v4** so that all the skilled craftsmen who were doing all the work on the sanctuary left their work
**v5** and said to Moses, "The people are bringing more than enough for doing the work the LORD has commanded us to do."

**v6** After Moses had given an order, they sent a proclamation throughout the camp: "No man or woman should make anything else as an offering for the sanctuary." So the people were restrained from bringing more,
**v7** since what they already had was more than enough to perform all the work.
#### The Ten Curtains for the Tabernacle

**v8** All the skilled craftsmen among the workmen made the ten curtains for the tabernacle. They were made of finely spun linen, as well as blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, with cherubim skillfully worked into them.
**v9** Each curtain was twenty-eight cubits long and four cubits wide; [^1] all the curtains were the same size.
**v10** And he joined five of the curtains together, and the other five he joined as well.

**v11** He made loops of blue material on the edge of the end curtain in the first set, and also on the end curtain in the second set.
**v12** He made fifty loops on one curtain and fifty loops on the end curtain of the second set, so that the loops lined up opposite one another.
**v13** He also made fifty gold clasps to join the curtains together, so that the tabernacle was a unit.
#### The Eleven Curtains of Goat Hair

**v14** He then made curtains of goat hair for the tent over the tabernacle—eleven curtains in all.
**v15** Each of the eleven curtains was the same size—thirty cubits long and four cubits wide. [^2]
**v16** He joined five of the curtains into one set and the other six into another.
**v17** He made fifty loops along the edge of the end curtain in the first set, and fifty loops along the edge of the corresponding curtain in the second set.
**v18** He also made fifty bronze clasps to join the tent together as a unit.

**v19** Additionally, he made for the tent a covering of ram skins dyed red, and over that a covering of fine leather. [^3]
#### The Frames and Bases

**v20** Next, he constructed upright frames of acacia wood for the tabernacle.
**v21** Each frame was ten cubits long and a cubit and a half wide. [^4]
**v22** Two tenons [^5] were connected to each other for each frame. He made all the frames of the tabernacle in this way.

**v23** He constructed twenty frames for the south side of the tabernacle,
**v24** with forty silver bases to put under the twenty frames—two bases for each frame, one under each tenon.

**v25** For the second side of the tabernacle, the north side, he made twenty frames
**v26** and forty silver bases—two bases under each frame.

**v27** He made six frames for the rear of the tabernacle, the west side,
**v28** and two frames for the two back corners of the tabernacle,
**v29** coupled together from bottom to top and fitted into a single ring. He made both corners in this way.
**v30** So there were eight frames and sixteen silver bases—two under each frame.

**v31** He also made five crossbars of acacia wood for the frames on one side of the tabernacle,
**v32** five for those on the other side, and five for those on the rear side of the tabernacle, to the west.

**v33** He made the central crossbar to run through the center of the frames, from one end to the other.
**v34** And he overlaid the frames with gold and made gold rings to hold the crossbars. He also overlaid the crossbars with gold.
#### The Veil

**v35** Next, he made the veil of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen, with cherubim skillfully worked into it.

**v36** He also made four posts of acacia wood for it and overlaid them with gold, along with gold hooks; and he cast four silver bases for the posts.
#### The Curtain for the Entrance

**v37** For the entrance to the tent, he made a curtain embroidered with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen,
**v38** together with five posts and their hooks.He overlaid the tops of the posts and their bands with gold, and their five bases were bronze.
[^1]: Each of the ten curtains was approximately 42 feet long and 6 feet wide (12.8 meters long and 1.8 meters wide). ( 36:9)
[^2]: Each of the eleven curtains was approximately 45 feet long and 6 feet wide (13.7 meters long and 1.8 meters wide). ( 36:15)
[^3]: Possibly the hides of large aquatic mammals ( 36:19)
[^4]: Each frame was approximately 15 feet long and 2.25 feet wide (4.6 meters long and 68.6 centimeters wide). ( 36:21)
[^5]: That is, projecting pieces of wood made for insertion into another piece; similarly in verse 24. ( 36:22)

### Chapter 37

#### Constructing the Ark
**v1** Bezalel went on to construct the ark of acacia wood, two and a half cubits long, a cubit and a half wide, and a cubit and a half high. [^1]
**v2** He overlaid it with pure gold, both inside and out, and made a gold molding around it.
**v3** And he cast four gold rings for its four feet, two rings on one side and two on the other.
**v4** Then he made poles of acacia wood and overlaid them with gold.
**v5** He inserted the poles into the rings on the sides of the ark in order to carry it.
#### The Mercy Seat

**v6** He constructed a mercy seat of pure gold, two and a half cubits long and a cubit and a half wide. [^2]
**v7** He made two cherubim of hammered gold at the ends of the mercy seat,
**v8** one cherub on one end and one on the other, all made from one piece of gold.
**v9** And the cherubim had wings that spread upward, overshadowing the mercy seat. The cherubim faced each other, looking toward the mercy seat.
#### The Table of Showbread

**v10** He also made the table of acacia wood two cubits long, a cubit wide, and a cubit and a half high. [^3]
**v11** He overlaid it with pure gold and made a gold molding around it.
**v12** And he made a rim around it a handbreadth wide [^4] and put a gold molding on the rim.

**v13** He cast four gold rings for the table and fastened them to the four corners at its four legs.
**v14** The rings were placed close to the rim, to serve as holders for the poles used to carry the table.
**v15** He made the poles of acacia wood for carrying the table and overlaid them with gold.

**v16** He also made the utensils for the table out of pure gold: its plates and dishes, as well as its bowls and pitchers for pouring drink offerings.
#### The Lampstand

**v17** Then he made the lampstand out of pure hammered gold, all of one piece: its base and shaft, its cups, and its buds and petals.
**v18** Six branches extended from the sides, three on one side and three on the other.
**v19** There were three cups shaped like almond blossoms on the first branch, each with buds and petals, three on the next branch, and the same for all six branches that extended from the lampstand.

**v20** And on the lampstand were four cups shaped like almond blossoms with buds and petals.
**v21** A bud was under the first pair of branches that extended from the lampstand, a bud under the second pair, and a bud under the third pair.
**v22** The buds and branches were all of one piece with the lampstand, hammered out of pure gold.

**v23** He also made its seven lamps, its wick trimmers, and trays of pure gold.
**v24** He made the lampstand and all its utensils from a talent of pure gold. [^5]
#### The Altar of Incense

**v25** He made the altar of incense out of acacia wood. It was square, a cubit long, a cubit wide, and two cubits high. [^6] Its horns were of one piece.
**v26** And he overlaid with pure gold the top and all the sides and horns. Then he made a molding of gold around it.

**v27** He made two gold rings below the molding on opposite sides to hold the poles used to carry it.
**v28** And he made the poles of acacia wood and overlaid them with gold.

**v29** He also made the sacred anointing oil and the pure, fragrant incense, the work of a perfumer.
[^1]: The ark was approximately 3.75 feet long, 2.25 feet wide, and 2.25 feet high (114.3 centimeters long, 68.6 centimeters wide, and 68.6 centimeters high). ( 37:1)
[^2]: The mercy seat was approximately 3.75 feet long and 2.25 feet wide (114.3 centimeters long and 68.6 centimeters wide). ( 37:6)
[^3]: The table was approximately 3 feet long, 1.5 feet wide, and 2.25 feet high (91.4 centimeters long, 45.7 centimeters wide, and 68.6 centimeters high). ( 37:10)
[^4]: A handbreadth is approximately 2.9 inches or 7.4 centimeters. ( 37:12)
[^5]: A talent is approximately 75.4 pounds or 34.2 kilograms of gold. ( 37:24)
[^6]: The altar was approximately 1.5 feet in length and width, and 3 feet high (45.7 centimeters in length and width, and 91.4 centimeters high). ( 37:25)

### Chapter 38

#### The Bronze Altar
**v1** Bezalel constructed [^1] the altar of burnt offering from acacia wood. It was square, five cubits long, five cubits wide, and three cubits high. [^2]
**v2** He made a horn at each of its four corners, so that the horns and altar were of one piece, and he overlaid the altar with bronze.

**v3** He made all the altar's utensils of bronze—its pots, shovels, sprinkling bowls, meat forks, and firepans.
**v4** He made a grate of bronze mesh for the altar under its ledge, halfway up from the bottom.

**v5** At the four corners of the bronze grate he cast four rings as holders for the poles.
**v6** And he made the poles of acacia wood and overlaid them with bronze.
**v7** Then he inserted the poles into the rings on the sides of the altar for carrying it. He made the altar with boards so that it was hollow.
#### The Bronze Basin

**v8** Next he made the bronze basin and its stand from the mirrors of the women who served at the entrance to the Tent of Meeting.
#### The Courtyard

**v9** Then he constructed the courtyard. The south side of the courtyard was a hundred cubits long [^3] and had curtains of finely spun linen,
**v10** with twenty posts and twenty bronze bases, and with silver hooks and bands on the posts.
**v11** The north side was also a hundred cubits long, with twenty posts and twenty bronze bases. The hooks and bands of the posts were silver.
**v12** The west side was fifty cubits long [^4] and had curtains, with ten posts and ten bases. The hooks and bands of the posts were silver.
**v13** And the east side, toward the sunrise, was also fifty cubits long.

**v14** The curtains on one side of the entrance were fifteen cubits long, [^5] with three posts and three bases.
**v15** And the curtains on the other side were also fifteen cubits long, with three posts and three bases as well.
**v16** All the curtains around the courtyard were made of finely spun linen.
**v17** The bases for the posts were bronze, the hooks and bands were silver, and the plating for the tops of the posts was silver. So all the posts of the courtyard were banded with silver.

**v18** The curtain for the entrance to the courtyard was embroidered with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and finely spun linen. It was twenty cubits long [^6] and, like the curtains of the courtyard, five cubits high, [^7]
**v19** with four posts and four bronze bases. Their hooks were silver, as well as the bands and the plating of their tops.
**v20** All the tent pegs for the tabernacle and for the surrounding courtyard were bronze.
#### An Inventory of Materials

**v21** This is the inventory for the tabernacle, the tabernacle of the Testimony, as recorded at Moses' command by the Levites under the direction of Ithamar son of Aaron the priest.
**v22** Bezalel son of Uri, the son of Hur, of the tribe of Judah, made everything that the LORD had commanded Moses.
**v23** With him was Oholiab son of Ahisamach, of the tribe of Dan, an engraver, designer, and embroiderer in blue, purple, and scarlet yarn and fine linen.

**v24** All the gold from the wave offering used for the work on the sanctuary totaled 29 talents and 730 shekels, [^8] according to the sanctuary shekel.

**v25** The silver from those numbered among the congregation totaled 100 talents and 1,775 shekels, [^9] according to the sanctuary shekel—
**v26** a beka per person, that is, half a shekel, [^10] according to the sanctuary shekel, from everyone twenty years of age or older who had crossed over to be numbered, a total of 603,550 men.

**v27** The hundred talents of silver [^11] were used to cast the bases of the sanctuary and the bases of the veil—100 bases from the 100 talents, one talent per base.

**v28** With the 1,775 shekels of silver [^12] he made the hooks for the posts, overlaid their tops, and supplied bands for them.

**v29** The bronze from the wave offering totaled 70 talents and 2,400 shekels. [^13]
**v30** He used it to make the bases for the entrance to the Tent of Meeting, the bronze altar and its bronze grating, all the utensils for the altar,
**v31** the bases for the surrounding courtyard and its gate, and all the tent pegs for the tabernacle and its surrounding courtyard.
[^1]: Literally He constructed ( 38:1)
[^2]: The altar was approximately 7.5 feet in length and width, and 4.5 feet high (2.3 meters in length and width, and 1.4 meters high). ( 38:1)
[^3]: 100 cubits is approximately 150 feet or 45.7 meters. ( 38:9)
[^4]: 50 cubits is approximately 75 feet or 22.9 meters. ( 38:12)
[^5]: 15 cubits is approximately 22.5 feet or 6.9 meters. ( 38:14)
[^6]: 20 cubits is approximately 30 feet or 9.1 meters. ( 38:18)
[^7]: 5 cubits is approximately 7.5 feet or 2.3 meters. ( 38:18)
[^8]: The total weight of the gold was approximately 1.1 tons or 1 metric ton. ( 38:24)
[^9]: The total weight of the silver was approximately 3.79 tons or 3.44 metric tons. ( 38:25)
[^10]: A beka is half a shekel, or approximately 0.2 ounces or 5.7 grams. ( 38:26)
[^11]: 100 talents is approximately 3.77 tons or 3.42 metric tons of silver. ( 38:27)
[^12]: 1,775 shekels is approximately 44.6 pounds or 20.2 kilograms of silver. ( 38:28)
[^13]: The total weight of the bronze was approximately 2.67 tons or 2.42 metric tons. ( 38:29)

### Chapter 39

#### The Ephod
**v1** From the blue, purple, and scarlet yarn they made specially woven garments for ministry in the sanctuary, as well as the holy garments for Aaron, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v2** Bezalel made [^1] the ephod of finely spun linen embroidered with gold, and with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn.
**v3** They hammered out thin sheets of gold and cut threads from them to interweave with the blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and fine linen—the work of a skilled craftsman.
**v4** They made shoulder pieces for the ephod, which were attached at two of its corners, so it could be fastened.
**v5** And the skillfully woven waistband of the ephod was of one piece with the ephod, of the same workmanship—with gold, with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and with finely spun linen, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v6** They mounted the onyx stones in gold filigree settings, engraved like a seal with the names of the sons of Israel.
**v7** Then they fastened them on the shoulder pieces of the ephod as memorial stones for the sons of Israel, as the LORD had commanded Moses.
#### The Breastpiece

**v8** He made the breastpiece with the same workmanship as the ephod, with gold, with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, and with finely spun linen.
**v9** It was square when folded over double, a span long and a span wide. [^2]

**v10** And they mounted on it four rows of gemstones: [^3] The first row had a ruby, a topaz, and an emerald;

**v11** the second row had a turquoise, a sapphire, and a diamond;

**v12** the third row had a jacinth, an agate, and an amethyst;

**v13** and the fourth row had a beryl, an onyx, and a jasper.These stones were mounted in gold filigree settings.

**v14** The twelve stones corresponded to the names of the sons of Israel. Each stone was engraved like a seal with the name of one of the twelve tribes.

**v15** For the breastpiece they made braided chains like cords of pure gold.
**v16** They also made two gold filigree settings and two gold rings, and fastened the two rings to the two corners of the breastpiece.
**v17** Then they fastened the two gold chains to the two gold rings at the corners of the breastpiece,
**v18** and they fastened the other ends of the two chains to the two filigree settings, attaching them to the shoulder pieces of the ephod at the front.

**v19** They made two more gold rings and attached them to the other two corners of the breastpiece, on the inside edge next to the ephod.

**v20** They made two additional gold rings and attached them to the bottom of the two shoulder pieces of the ephod, on its front, near the seam just above its woven waistband.
**v21** Then they tied the rings of the breastpiece to the rings of the ephod with a cord of blue yarn, so that the breastpiece was above the waistband of the ephod and would not swing out from the ephod, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.
#### Additional Priestly Garments

**v22** They made the robe of the ephod entirely of blue cloth, the work of a weaver,
**v23** with an opening in the center of the robe like that of a garment, [^4] with a collar around the opening so that it would not tear.

**v24** They made pomegranates of blue, purple, and scarlet yarn and finely spun linen on the lower hem of the robe.
**v25** They also made bells of pure gold and attached them around the hem between the pomegranates,
**v26** alternating the bells and pomegranates around the lower hem of the robe to be worn for ministry, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v27** For Aaron and his sons they made tunics of fine linen, the work of a weaver,
**v28** as well as the turban of fine linen, the ornate headbands and undergarments of finely spun linen,
**v29** and the sash of finely spun linen, embroidered with blue, purple, and scarlet yarn, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v30** They also made the plate of the holy crown of pure gold, and they engraved on it, like an inscription on a seal:HOLY TO THE LORD. [^5]

**v31** Then they fastened to it a blue cord to mount it on the turban, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.
#### Moses Approves the Work

**v32** So all the work for the tabernacle, the Tent of Meeting, was completed. The Israelites did everything just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v33** Then they brought the tabernacle to Moses:the tent with all its furnishings, its clasps, its frames, its crossbars, and its posts and bases;

**v34** the covering of ram skins dyed red, the covering of fine leather, [^6] and the veil of the covering;

**v35** the ark of the Testimony [^7] with its poles and the mercy seat;

**v36** the table with all its utensils and the Bread of the Presence;

**v37** the pure gold lampstand with its row of lamps and all its utensils, as well as the oil for the light;

**v38** the gold altar, the anointing oil, the fragrant incense, and the curtain for the entrance to the tent;

**v39** the bronze altar with its bronze grating, its poles, and all its utensils; the basin with its stand;

**v40** the curtains of the courtyard with its posts and bases; the curtain for the gate of the courtyard, its ropes and tent pegs, and all the equipment for the service of the tabernacle, the Tent of Meeting;

**v41** and the woven garments for ministering in the sanctuary, both the holy garments for Aaron the priest and the garments for his sons to serve as priests.

**v42** The Israelites had done all the work just as the LORD had commanded Moses.
**v43** And Moses inspected all the work and saw that they had accomplished it just as the LORD had commanded. So Moses blessed them.
[^1]: Literally He made ( 39:2)
[^2]: The breastpiece, when folded over, was approximately 9 inches or 22.9 centimeters in both length and width. ( 39:9)
[^3]: The precise identification of some of these gemstones is uncertain. ( 39:10)
[^4]: The meaning of the Hebrew word is uncertain; possibly a coat of mail. ( 39:23)
[^5]: That is, the LORD ( 39:30)
[^6]: Possibly the hides of large aquatic mammals ( 39:34)
[^7]: That is, the ark of the covenant ( 39:35)

### Chapter 40

#### Setting Up the Tabernacle
**v1** Then the LORD said to Moses,
**v2** "On the first day of the first month you are to set up the tabernacle, the Tent of Meeting.
**v3** Put the ark of the Testimony [^1] in it and screen off the ark with the veil.
**v4** Then bring in the table and set out its arrangement; bring in the lampstand as well, and set up its lamps.

**v5** Place the gold altar of incense in front of the ark of the Testimony, and hang the curtain at the entrance to the tabernacle.
**v6** Place the altar of burnt offering in front of the entrance to the tabernacle, the Tent of Meeting.
**v7** And place the basin between the Tent of Meeting and the altar, and put water in it.

**v8** Set up the surrounding courtyard and hang the curtain for the entrance to the courtyard.

**v9** Take the anointing oil and anoint the tabernacle and everything in it; consecrate it along with all its furnishings, and it shall be holy.
**v10** Anoint the altar of burnt offering and all its utensils; consecrate the altar, and it shall be most holy.
**v11** Anoint the basin and its stand and consecrate them.

**v12** Then bring Aaron and his sons to the entrance to the Tent of Meeting and wash them with water.
**v13** And you are to clothe Aaron with the holy garments, anoint him, and consecrate him, so that he may serve Me as a priest.
**v14** Bring his sons forward and clothe them with tunics.
**v15** Anoint them just as you anointed their father, so that they may also serve Me as priests. Their anointing will qualify them for a permanent priesthood throughout their generations."

**v16** Moses did everything just as the LORD had commanded him.
**v17** So the tabernacle was set up on the first day of the first month of the second year.

**v18** When Moses set up the tabernacle, he laid its bases, positioned its frames, inserted its crossbars, and set up its posts.
**v19** Then he spread the tent over the tabernacle and put the covering over the tent, just as the LORD had commanded him.

**v20** Moses took the Testimony and placed it in the ark, attaching the poles to the ark; and he set the mercy seat atop the ark.
**v21** Then he brought the ark into the tabernacle, put up the veil for the screen, and shielded off the ark of the Testimony, just as the LORD had commanded him.

**v22** Moses placed the table in the Tent of Meeting on the north side of the tabernacle, outside the veil.
**v23** He arranged the bread on it before the LORD, just as the LORD had commanded him.

**v24** He also placed the lampstand in the Tent of Meeting opposite the table on the south side of the tabernacle
**v25** and set up the lamps before the LORD, just as the LORD had commanded him.

**v26** Moses placed the gold altar in the Tent of Meeting, in front of the veil,
**v27** and he burned fragrant incense on it, just as the LORD had commanded him.
**v28** Then he put up the curtain at the entrance to the tabernacle.
**v29** He placed the altar of burnt offering near the entrance to the tabernacle, the Tent of Meeting, and offered on it the burnt offering and the grain offering, just as the LORD had commanded him.

**v30** He placed the basin between the Tent of Meeting and the altar and put water in it for washing;
**v31** and from it Moses, Aaron, and his sons washed their hands and feet.
**v32** They washed whenever they entered the Tent of Meeting or approached the altar, just as the LORD had commanded Moses.

**v33** And Moses set up the courtyard around the tabernacle and the altar, and he hung the curtain for the entrance to the courtyard. So Moses finished the work.
#### The Cloud and the Glory

**v34** Then the cloud covered the Tent of Meeting, and the glory of the LORD filled the tabernacle.
**v35** Moses was unable to enter the Tent of Meeting because the cloud had settled on it, and the glory of the LORD filled the tabernacle.

**v36** Whenever the cloud was lifted from above the tabernacle, the Israelites would set out through all the stages of their journey.
**v37** If the cloud was not lifted, they would not set out until the day it was taken up.
